## **PART I** 

## **Item 1.Business** 

Oracle provides products and services that address enterprise informaïŋ―on technology (IT) environments. Our products and services include enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings that are delivered worldwide through a variety of flexible and interoperable IT deployment models. These models include on-premise deployments, cloud-based deployments, and hybrid deployments (an approach that combines both on-premise and cloud-based deployment) such as our Oracle Cloud@Customer offering (an instance of Oracle Cloud in a customerâs own data center). Accordingly, we offer choice and flexibility to our customers and facilitate the product, service and deployment combinaïŋ―ons that best suit our customersâ needs. Our customers include businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and resellers that we market and sell to directly through our worldwide sales force and indirectly through the Oracle Partner Network. Using Oracle technologies, our customers build, deploy, run, manage and support their internal and external products, services and business operaïŋ―ons including, for example, a global cloud applicaïŋ―ons developer that uïŋ―lizes Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (OCI) to power its soïŋ―ware-as-a-service (SaaS) offerings; a mulïŋ―-naïŋ―onal financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―on that runs its banking applicaïŋ―ons using the Oracle Exadata Database Machine; and a global consumer products company that leverages Oracle Fusion Cloud Enterprise Resource Planning for its accounïŋ―ng processes, consolidaïŋ―on and financial planning funcïŋ―ons. 

Oracle Cloud Services offerings, which include Oracle SaaS and OCI offerings, provide comprehensive and integrated applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure services delivered via cloud-based deployment models. Oracle Cloud Services integrate the IT components, including soïŋ―ware, hardware and services, on a customerâs behalf in a cloud-based IT environment that Oracle deploys, manages, supports and upgrades for the customer and that a customer may access uïŋ―lizing common web browsers via a broad spectrum of devices. 

Oracle Cloud Services are designed to be rapidly deployable to enable customers shorter ïŋ―me to innovaïŋ―on; intuiïŋ―ve for casual and experienced users; easily maintainable to reduce upgrade, integraïŋ―on and tesïŋ―ng work; connectable among differing deployment models to enable interchangeability and extendibility between IT environments; compaïŋ―ble to easily move workloads between the Oracle Cloud and other IT environments; cost-effecïŋ―ve by requiring lower upfront customer investment; and secure, standards-based and reliable. 

Oracle cloud license and on-premise license deployment offerings include Oracle Applicaïŋ―ons, Oracle Database and Oracle Middleware soïŋ―ware offerings, among others, which customers deploy using IT infrastructure from the Oracle Cloud or their own cloud-based or on-premise IT environments. Substanïŋ―ally all customers, at their opïŋ―on, purchase license support contracts when they purchase an Oracle license. 

Oracle hardware products include Oracle Engineered Systems, servers, storage and industry-specific products, among others. Customers generally opt to purchase hardware support contracts when they purchase Oracle hardware products. 

Oracle also offers services to assist our customers and partners to maximize the performance of their Oracle purchases. 

Providing choice and flexibility to Oracle customers as to when and how they deploy Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies is an important element of our corporate strategy. We believe that offering customers broad, comprehensive, flexible and interoperable deployment models for Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies is important to our growth strategy and beïŋ―er addresses customer needs relaïŋ―ve to our compeïŋ―tors, many of whom provide fewer offerings, more restricïŋ―ve deployment models and less flexibility for a customerâs transiïŋ―on to cloud-based IT environments. 

Our investments in, and innovaïŋ―on with respect to, Oracle products and services that we offer through our three businesses (cloud and license, hardware and services businesses, described further below) are another important element of our corporate strategy. In fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020, we invested $7.2 billion, $6.5 billion and $6.1 billion, respecïŋ―vely, in research and development to enhance our exisïŋ―ng porïŋ―olio of offerings and to develop new technologies and services. We have a deep understanding as to how applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies interact and funcïŋ―on with one another including through the use of OCI to power our Oracle Fusion SaaS Applicaïŋ―ons, which we and our customers use to run internal business processes. We focus our development efforts on improving the performance, security, operaïŋ―on, integraïŋ―on and cost-effecïŋ―veness of our offerings

## **Oracle Applicaïŋ―ons and Infrastructure Technologies** 

Oracleâs comprehensive porïŋ―olio of applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies is designed to address an organizaïŋ―onâs IT environment needs including business process, infrastructure and applicaïŋ―ons development requirements, among others. Oracle technologies are based upon industry standards and are designed to be enterprise-grade, reliable, scalable and secure. Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies including database and middleware soïŋ―ware as well as enterprise applicaïŋ―ons, virtualizaïŋ―on, clustering, large-scale systems management and related infrastructure products and services are the building blocks of Oracle Cloud Services, our partnersâ cloud services, and our customersâ cloud IT environments. Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings are marketed and sold through our cloud and license, hardware, and services businesses and are delivered through the Oracle Cloud, or through other IT deployment models including cloud-based, hybrid and on-premise deployments. We believe Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings enable flexibility, interoperability and choice to best meet customer IT needs. 

We believe that our Oracle Cloud Services offerings are opportuniïŋ―es for us to conïŋ―nue to expand our cloud and license business. ## _**Oracle Cloud Soïŋ―ware-as-a-Service (SaaS)**_ 

Oracleâs broad spectrum of Oracle Cloud SaaS offerings provides customers a choice of soïŋ―ware applicaïŋ―ons that are delivered via a cloud-based IT environment that we deploy, manage, upgrade and support, and that customers purchase by entering into a subscripïŋ―on agreement with us for a stated period. ## _**Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (OCI)**_ 

OCI offerings are based upon Oracleâs Next-Generaïŋ―on Cloud Infrastructure and are designed to deliver our infrastructure technologies as a service including compute, storage and networking services. OCI offerings include our Oracle Autonomous Database offerings, among others, that Oracle runs, manages, upgrades and supports on behalf of the customer. We typically charge a prepaid fee that is decremented as the OCI services are consumed by the customer over a stated ïŋ―me period. By uïŋ―lizing OCI, customers can leverage the Oracle Cloud for enterprise-grade, high performance, scalable, cost-effecïŋ―ve and secure infrastructure technologies that are designed to be rapidly deployable and provide real-ïŋ―me elasïŋ―city while reducing the amount of ïŋ―me and resources normally consumed by IT processes within on-premise environments. OCI is designed to be differenïŋ―ated from other cloud vendors to provide beïŋ―er security by separaïŋ―ng cloud control code computers from customer data compute nodes. Customers use OCI to build and operate new cloud-naïŋ―ve applicaïŋ―ons, to run new workloads and to move their exisïŋ―ng Oracle or non-Oracle workloads to the Oracle Cloud from their on-premise data centers or from other cloudbased IT environments, among other uses. We conïŋ―nue to invest in OCI to improve features and performance; to expand the catalog of cloud-based infrastructure tools and services that we provide; to increase the capacity and geographic footprint to deliver these services; to simplify the processes for migraïŋ―ng workloads to the Oracle Cloud; and to provide customers with the ability to run workloads across different IT environments, the Oracle Cloud as well as other third-party clouds in a hybrid deployment model. 

Oracle customers and partners uïŋ―lize OCI offerings for plaïŋ―orm-related services that are based upon the Oracle Database, Java and Oracle Middleware, including open source and other tools for a variety of use cases across data management (including the use of Oracle Autonomous Database and MySQL HeatWave), applicaïŋ―ons development, integraïŋ―on, content management, analyïŋ―cs, IT management and governance, security, and rapidly emerging technologies such as machine learning. OCI machine learning features are designed to be embedded into customer applicaïŋ―ons for a variety of predicïŋ―ve use cases including, among others, the servicing of machine parts that are at risk of failing, the stocking of retailer store shelves, and the financial modeling to stay within a businessâ forecasts. 

Oracle customers and partners also uïŋ―lize OCI offerings for highly-scalable, available, and secure compute, storage and networking services. OCI compute services range from virtual machines to graphics processing unit-based offerings to bare metal servers and include opïŋ―ons for dense I/O workloads and high performance compuïŋ―ng. OCI storage offerings include block, object and archive storage services. In addiïŋ―on, our OCI offerings include networking, connecïŋ―vity, and edge services that help connect customer data centers and third-party clouds, such as Microsoïŋ― Azure, with our OCI services for the creaïŋ―on of distributed and mulïŋ―-cloud architectures. 

In addiïŋ―on to the full suite of OCI offerings delivered by dozens of Oracle public cloud regions across the globe, we provide our customers with flexibility by offering certain OCI services within a customerâs own data center to address customer latency requirements and address restricïŋ―ons imposed upon customers that operate in certain regulated industries, enïŋ―ïŋ―es or jurisdicïŋ―ons. ## Oracle Autonomous Database

Oracle Autonomous Database is engineered to lower labor costs and reduce human error while using machine learning-driven diagnosïŋ―cs for fault predicïŋ―on and error handling and is also engineered to provide automaïŋ―c threat detecïŋ―on and remediaïŋ―on. ## **Item 1A.Risk Factors** 

We operate in rapidly changing economic and technological environments that present numerous risks, many of which are driven by factors that we cannot control or predict. The following discussion, as well as our âCriïŋ―cal Accounïŋ―ng Policies and Esïŋ―matesâ discussion in Item 7 Managementâs Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condiïŋ―on and Results of Operaïŋ―ons, highlights some of these risks. The risks described below are not exhausïŋ―ve and you should carefully consider these risks and uncertainïŋ―es before invesïŋ―ng in our securiïŋ―es. 

## **Business and Operaïŋ―onal Risks** 

_**Our success depends upon our ability to develop and sell new products and services, integrate acquired products and services and enhance our exisïŋ―ng products and services.**_ Rapid technological advances, intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on, changing delivery models and evolving standards in computer hardware and soïŋ―ware development and communicaïŋ―ons infrastructure, changing and increasingly sophisïŋ―cated customer needs and frequent new product introducïŋ―ons and enhancements characterize the industries in which we compete. If we are unable to develop new or sufficiently differenïŋ―ated products and services, enhance and improve our product offerings and support services in a ïŋ―mely manner or posiïŋ―on and price our products and services to meet demand, customers may not purchase or subscribe to our license, hardware or cloud offerings or renew license support, hardware support or cloud subscripïŋ―ons contracts. Renewals of these contracts are important to the growth of our business. In addiïŋ―on, we cannot provide any assurance that the standards on which we choose to develop new products will allow us to compete effecïŋ―vely for business opportuniïŋ―es in emerging areas. 

We have conïŋ―nued to refresh and release new offerings of our cloud products and services. Machine learning and arïŋ―ficial intelligence are increasingly driving innovaïŋ―ons in technology, but if they fail to operate as anïŋ―cipated or our other products do not perform as promised, our business and reputaïŋ―on may be harmed. 

During fiscal 2022, we held many of our major customer events in a virtual format. Our shiïŋ― to virtual customer events may not be successful, and we may not be able to showcase our products as well as we have historically done through in-person events or generate the same customer interest, opportuniïŋ―es and leads through these virtual events. We currently plan to reintroduce large in-person events during fiscal 2023 but we may not be able to do so successfully and our customers may not be able or willing to aïŋ―end them, which could adversely impact our ability to market and sell our products and services. 

In addiïŋ―on, our business may be adversely affected if: 

- we do not conïŋ―nue to develop and release new or enhanced products and services within the anïŋ―cipated ïŋ―me frames;

- infrastructure costs to deliver new or enhanced products and services take longer or result in greater costs than anïŋ―cipated;

_**Our Oracle Cloud strategy, including our Oracle Cloud Soïŋ―ware-as-a-Service and Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (SaaS and OCI, respecïŋ―vely, and collecïŋ―vely, Oracle Cloud Services) offerings, may adversely affect our revenues and profitability.**_ We provide our cloud and other offerings to customers worldwide via a variety of deployment models, including via our cloud-based SaaS and OCI offerings. Addiïŋ―onally, the increasing prevalence of cloud and SaaS delivery models offered by us and our compeïŋ―tors may unfavorably impact the pricing of our cloud and license offerings. As customer demand for our cloud offerings increases, we experience volaïŋ―lity in our reported revenues and operaïŋ―ng results due to the differences in ïŋ―ming of revenue recogniïŋ―on between our cloud license and on-premise license, and hardware product arrangements relaïŋ―ve to our cloud offering arrangements. Customers predominantly purchase our cloud offerings on a subscripïŋ―on basis and revenues from these offerings are generally recognized ratably or as services are consumed over the terms of the subscripïŋ―ons. Consequently, any deterioraïŋ―on in sales acïŋ―vity associated with our cloud offerings may not be immediately observable in our consolidated statement of operaïŋ―ons. This is in contrast to revenues associated with our license and hardware product arrangements, which are generally recognized in full at the ïŋ―me of delivery of the related licenses and hardware products. In addiïŋ―on, we may not be able to accurately anïŋ―cipate customer transiïŋ―ons from or be able to sufficiently backfill reduced customer demand for our license, hardware and support offerings relaïŋ―ve to the expected increase in customer adopïŋ―on of and demand for our Oracle Cloud Services, which could adversely affect our revenues and profitability. 

As a part of our Oracle Cloud strategy, we plan our investment levels based on esïŋ―mates of future revenues and future anïŋ―cipated rates of growth. In recent periods, our cloud services and license support expenses have grown to meet current and expected demand for our cloud offerings, including investments to increase our exisïŋ―ng data center capacity and to establish data centers in new geographic locaïŋ―ons. In connecïŋ―on with these investments, we entered, and expect to conïŋ―nue to enter, into long-term operaïŋ―ng lease commitments with third party data center providers that generally require us to pay fees to early exit such obligaïŋ―ons should our strategies change, which could adversely impact our profitability and cash flows. In addiïŋ―on, we ouïŋ―it these data centers with equipment and improvements that we typically depreciate over their esïŋ―mated useful lives, which could be shortened should our cloud strategies change, which could adversely affect our profitability. 

_**We might experience significant coding, manufacturing or configuraïŋ―on errors in our cloud, license and hardware offerings.**_ Despite tesïŋ―ng prior to the release and throughout the lifecycle of a product or service, our cloud, license and hardware offerings someïŋ―mes contain coding, manufacturing or configuraïŋ―on errors that can impact their funcïŋ―on, performance and security, and result in other negaïŋ―ve consequences. _**If we are unable to compete effecïŋ―vely, the results of operaïŋ―ons and prospects for our business could be harmed.**_ We face intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on in all aspects of our business. The nature of the IT industry creates a compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve landscape that is constantly evolving as firms emerge, expand or are acquired, as technology evolves and as delivery models change. Many vendors spend amounts in excess of what Oracle spends to develop and market applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies including databases, middleware products, applicaïŋ―on development tools, business applicaïŋ―ons, collaboraïŋ―on products and business intelligence, compute, storage and networking products, among others, which compete with Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings. Mergers, consolidaïŋ―ons or alliances among our compeïŋ―tors, or acquisiïŋ―ons of our compeïŋ―tors by large companies may result in increased compeïŋ―ïŋ―on. We may also face increasing compeïŋ―ïŋ―on from open source soïŋ―ware iniïŋ―aïŋ―ves in which compeïŋ―tors may provide soïŋ―ware and intellectual property for free. Exisïŋ―ng or new compeïŋ―tors could gain sales opportuniïŋ―es or customers at our expense. 

_**We may need to change our pricing models to compete successfully.**_ The intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on we face in the sales of our products and services and general economic and business condiïŋ―ons could put pressure on us to change our prices. If our compeïŋ―tors offer deep discounts on certain products or services or develop products that the marketplace considers more valuable, we may need to lower prices, introduce pricing models and offerings that are less favorable to us, or offer other favorable terms in order to compete successfully. Any such changes may reduce revenues and margins and could adversely affect operaïŋ―ng results. Addiïŋ―onally, the increasing prevalence of cloud delivery models offered by us and our compeïŋ―tors may unfavorably impact the pricing of our other cloud and license, hardware and services offerings, and we may also incur increased cloud delivery expenses as we expand our cloud operaïŋ―ons and update our infrastructure, all of which could reduce our revenues and/or profitability. Our license support fees and hardware support fees are generally priced as a percentage of our net license fees and net new hardware products fees, respecïŋ―vely. Our compeïŋ―tors may offer lower pricing on their support offerings, which could put pressure on us to further discount our offerings. 

Changes to our prices and pricing policies could cause our revenues to decline or be delayed as our sales force implements and our customers adjust to the new pricing policies. - non-pracïŋ―cing enïŋ―ïŋ―es conïŋ―nue to assert intellectual property infringement in our industry segments.

## **General Risks** 

_**Economic, poliïŋ―cal and market condiïŋ―ons can adversely affect our business, results of operaïŋ―ons and financial condiïŋ―on, including our revenue growth and profitability, which in turn could adversely affect our stock price.**_ Our business is influenced by a range of factors that are beyond our control and that we have no comparaïŋ―ve advantage in forecasïŋ―ng. - general economic and business condiïŋ―ons;

- governmental budgetary constraints or shiïŋ―s in government spending prioriïŋ―es; and

## **Business Overview** 

Oracle provides products and services that address enterprise informaïŋ―on technology (IT) environments. Our products and services include enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings that are delivered worldwide through a variety of flexible and interoperable IT deployment models. These models include on-premise deployments, cloud-based deployments, and hybrid deployments (an approach that combines both on-premise and cloud-based deployments). Accordingly, we offer choice and flexibility to our customers and facilitate the product, service and deployment combinaïŋ―ons that best suit our customersâ needs. Through our worldwide sales force and Oracle Partner Network, we sell to customers all over the world including businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and resellers. 

We have three businesses: cloud and license; hardware; and services; each of which comprises a single operaïŋ―ng segment. The descripïŋ―ons set forth below as a part of this Item 7 Managementâs Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condiïŋ―on and Results of Operaïŋ―ons and the informaïŋ―on contained within Item 1 Business and Note 14 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements included elsewhere in this Annual Report provide addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on related to our businesses and operaïŋ―ng segments and align to how our chief operaïŋ―ng decision makers (CODMs), which include our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer and Chief Technology Officer, view our operaïŋ―ng results and allocate resources. 

## **Cloud and License Business** 

Our cloud and license business, which represented 85% and 84% of our total revenues in fiscal 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely, markets, sells and delivers a broad spectrum of enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies through our cloud and license offerings. Revenue streams included in our cloud and license business are: 

- Cloud services and license support revenues, which include: 

   - license support revenues, which are earned by providing Oracle license support services to customers that have elected to purchase support services in connecïŋ―on with the purchase of Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure soïŋ―ware licenses for use in cloud, on-premise and other IT environments. Substanïŋ―ally all license support customers renew their support contracts with us upon expiraïŋ―on in order to conïŋ―nue to benefit from technical support services and the periodic issuance of unspecified updates and enhancements, which current license support customers are enïŋ―tled to receive. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net fees paid by the customer to purchase a cloud license and/or on-premise license; are generally billed in advance of the support services being performed; are generally renewed at the customerâs opïŋ―on; and are generally recognized as revenues ratably over the contractual period that the support services are provided, which is generally one year; and 

   - cloud services revenues, which provide customers access to Oracle Cloud applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies via cloud-based deployment models that Oracle develops, provides unspecified updates and enhancements for, deploys, hosts, manages and supports and that

- Cloud license and on-premise license revenues, which include revenues from the licensing of our soïŋ―ware products including Oracle Applicaïŋ―ons, Oracle Database, Oracle Middleware and Java, among others, which our customers deploy within cloud-based, on-premise and other IT environments. ## **Hardware Business**

## **Criïŋ―cal Accounïŋ―ng Policies and Esïŋ―mates**

GAAP, as set forth within the ASC, requires us to make certain esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons. We believe that the esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons upon which we rely are reasonable based upon informaïŋ―on available to us at the ïŋ―me that these esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons are made. These esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons can affect the reported amounts of assets and liabiliïŋ―es as of the date of the financial statements as well as the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the periods presented. To the extent that there are differences between these esïŋ―mates, judgments or assumpïŋ―ons and actual results, our financial statements will be affected. The accounïŋ―ng policies that reflect our more significant esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons and which we believe are the most criïŋ―cal to aid in fully understanding and evaluaïŋ―ng our reported financial results include: 

- Revenue Recogniïŋ―on; 

- Business Combinaïŋ―ons; 

- Goodwill and Intangible AssetsâImpairment Assessments; 

- Accounïŋ―ng for Income Taxes; and 

- Legal and Other Conïŋ―ngencies.

Note 1 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements included elsewhere in this Annual Report includes addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on about our criïŋ―cal and other accounïŋ―ng policies. 

## _**Revenue Recogniïŋ―on**_ 

The most criïŋ―cal judgments required in applying ASC 606, _Revenue Recogniïŋ―on from Customers_ , and our revenue recogniïŋ―on policy relate to the determinaïŋ―on of disïŋ―nct performance obligaïŋ―ons and the evaluaïŋ―on of the standalone selling price (SSP) for each performance obligaïŋ―on. 

39 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

Many of our customer contracts include mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons. Judgment is required in determining whether each performance obligaïŋ―on within a customer contract is disïŋ―nct. Oracle products and services generally funcïŋ―on on a standalone basis and do not require a significant amount of integraïŋ―on or interdependency. Therefore, mulïŋ―ple products and services contained within a customer contract are generally considered to be disïŋ―nct and are not combined for revenue recogniïŋ―on purposes. We allocate the transacïŋ―on price for each customer contract to each performance obligaïŋ―on based on the relaïŋ―ve SSP (the determinaïŋ―on of SSP is discussed below) for each performance obligaïŋ―on within each contract. We recognize the amount of transacïŋ―on price allocated to each performance obligaïŋ―on within a customer contract as revenue as each performance obligaïŋ―on is saïŋ―sfied. 

We use historical sales transacïŋ―on data and judgment, among other factors, in determining the SSP for products and services. For substanïŋ―ally all performance obligaïŋ―ons except cloud licenses and on-premise licenses, we are able to establish the SSP based on the observable prices of products or services sold separately in comparable circumstances to similar customers. We typically establish an SSP range for our products and services, which is reassessed on a periodic basis or when facts and circumstances change. SSP for our products and services can evolve over ïŋ―me due to changes in our pricing pracïŋ―ces that are influenced by intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on, changes in demand for our products and services, and economic factors, among others. Our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses have not historically been sold on a standalone basis, as substanïŋ―ally all customers elect to purchase license support contracts at the ïŋ―me of a license purchase. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net fees paid by the customer to purchase the license. We are unable to establish the SSP for our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses based on observable prices given the same products are sold for a broad range of amounts (that is, the selling price is highly variable) and a representaïŋ―ve SSP is not discernible from past transacïŋ―ons or other observable evidence. As a result, the SSP for a cloud license and an on-premise license included in a contract with mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons is generally determined by applying a residual approach whereby all other performance obligaïŋ―ons within a contract are first allocated a porïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price based upon their respecïŋ―ve SSPs, with any residual amount of transacïŋ―on price allocated to cloud license and on-premise license revenues. 

## _**Business Combinaïŋ―ons**_ 

We apply the provisions of ASC 805, _Business Combinaïŋ―ons_ (ASC 805), in accounïŋ―ng for our acquisiïŋ―ons. ASC 805 requires that we evaluate whether a transacïŋ―on pertains to an acquisiïŋ―on of assets, or to an acquisiïŋ―on of a business. A business is defined as an integrated set of assets and acïŋ―viïŋ―es that is capable of being conducted and managed for the purpose of providing a return to investors. Asset acquisiïŋ―ons are accounted for by allocaïŋ―ng the cost of the acquisiïŋ―on to the individual assets and liabiliïŋ―es assumed on a relaïŋ―ve fair value basis; whereas the acquisiïŋ―on of a business requires us to recognize separately from goodwill the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values. Goodwill as of the acquisiïŋ―on date is measured as the excess of consideraïŋ―on transferred over the net of the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values of the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed. While we use our best esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons to accurately value assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the acquisiïŋ―on date as well as any conïŋ―ngent consideraïŋ―on, where applicable, our esïŋ―mates are inherently uncertain and subject to refinement. As a result, during the measurement period, which may be up to one year from the business acquisiïŋ―on date, we record adjustments to the assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed with the corresponding offset to goodwill. Upon the conclusion of a business acquisiïŋ―onâs measurement period or final determinaïŋ―on of the values of assets acquired or liabiliïŋ―es assumed, whichever comes first, any subsequent adjustments are recorded to our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. 

Accounïŋ―ng for business combinaïŋ―ons requires our management to make significant esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons, especially at the acquisiïŋ―on date, including our esïŋ―mates for intangible assets, pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngencies and any conïŋ―ngent consideraïŋ―on, where applicable. Although we believe that the assumpïŋ―ons and esïŋ―mates we have made in the past have been reasonable and appropriate, they are based in part on historical experience and informaïŋ―on obtained from the management of the acquired companies and are inherently uncertain. Unanïŋ―cipated events and circumstances may occur that may affect the accuracy or validity of such assumpïŋ―ons, esïŋ―mates or actual results.

For a given business acquisiïŋ―on, we may idenïŋ―fy certain pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngencies as of the acquisiïŋ―on date and may extend our review and evaluaïŋ―on of these pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngencies throughout the measurement period in order to obtain sufficient informaïŋ―on to assess whether we include these conïŋ―ngencies as a part of the fair value esïŋ―mates of assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed and, if so, to determine their esïŋ―mated amounts.

## _**Goodwill and Intangible AssetsâImpairment Assessments**_ 

We review goodwill for impairment annually and whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate its carrying value may not be recoverable. We make certain judgments and assumpïŋ―ons to determine our reporïŋ―ng units and in allocaïŋ―ng shared assets and liabiliïŋ―es to determine the carrying values for each of our reporïŋ―ng units. 

Judgment in the assessment of qualitaïŋ―ve factors of impairment include cost factors; financial performance; legal, regulatory, contractual, poliïŋ―cal, business, and other factors; enïŋ―ty specific factors; industry and market consideraïŋ―ons, macroeconomic condiïŋ―ons, and other relevant events and factors affecïŋ―ng the reporïŋ―ng unit. To the extent we determine that it is more likely than not that the fair value of the reporïŋ―ng unit is less than its carrying value, a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve test is then performed. 

Performing a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve goodwill impairment test includes the determinaïŋ―on of the fair value of a reporïŋ―ng unit and involves significant esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons. These esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons include, among others, revenue growth rates and operaïŋ―ng margins used to calculate projected future cash flows, risk-adjusted discount rates, future economic and market condiïŋ―ons, and the determinaïŋ―on of appropriate market comparables. 

We make judgments about the recoverability of purchased finite lived intangible assets whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that impairment may exist. In such situaïŋ―ons, we are required to evaluate whether the net book values of our finite lived intangible assets are recoverable. We determine whether finite lived intangible assets are recoverable based upon the forecasted future cash flows that are expected to be generated by the lowest level associated asset grouping. Assumpïŋ―ons and esïŋ―mates about future values and remaining useful lives of our intangible assets are complex and subjecïŋ―ve and include, among others, forecasted undiscounted cash flows to be generated by certain asset groupings. These assumpïŋ―ons and esïŋ―mates can be affected by a variety of factors, including external factors such as industry and economic trends and internal factors such as changes in our business strategy and our internal forecasts. 

## _**Accounïŋ―ng for Income Taxes**_ 

Judgment is required in determining our worldwide income tax provision. In the ordinary course of a global business, there are many transacïŋ―ons and calculaïŋ―ons where the ulïŋ―mate tax outcome is uncertain. Some of these uncertainïŋ―es arise as a consequence of revenue sharing and cost reimbursement arrangements among related enïŋ―ïŋ―es, the process of idenïŋ―fying items of revenues and expenses that qualify for preferenïŋ―al tax 

41 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

treatment, and the segregaïŋ―on of foreign and domesïŋ―c earnings and expenses to avoid double taxaïŋ―on. Although we believe that our esïŋ―mates are reasonable, the final tax outcome of these maïŋ―ers could be different from that which is reflected in our historical income tax provisions and accruals. Such differences could have a material effect on our income tax provision and net income in the period in which such determinaïŋ―on is made. 

We record a valuaïŋ―on allowance to reduce our deferred tax assets to the amount that is more likely than not to be realized. In order for us to realize our deferred tax assets, we must be able to generate sufficient taxable income in those jurisdicïŋ―ons where the deferred tax assets are located. We consider future growth, forecasted earnings, future taxable income, the mix of earnings in the jurisdicïŋ―ons in which we operate, historical earnings, taxable income in prior years, if carryback is permiïŋ―ed under the law, and prudent and feasible tax planning strategies in determining the need for a valuaïŋ―on allowance. In the event we were to determine that we would not be able to realize all or part of our net deferred tax assets in the future, an adjustment to the deferred tax assets valuaïŋ―on allowance would be charged to earnings in the period in which we make such a determinaïŋ―on, or goodwill would be adjusted at our final determinaïŋ―on of the valuaïŋ―on allowance related to an acquisiïŋ―on within the measurement period. If we later determine that it is more likely than not that the net deferred tax assets would be realized, we would reverse the applicable porïŋ―on of the previously provided valuaïŋ―on allowance as an adjustment to our provision for income taxes at such ïŋ―me. 

We calculate our current and deferred tax provision based on esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons that could differ from the actual results reflected in income tax returns filed during the subsequent year. Adjustments based on filed returns are generally recorded in the period when the tax returns are filed and the global tax implicaïŋ―ons are known, which can materially impact our effecïŋ―ve tax rate. 

The amount of income tax we pay is subject to ongoing audits by federal, state and foreign tax authoriïŋ―es, which oïŋ―en result in proposed assessments. Our esïŋ―mate of the potenïŋ―al outcome for any uncertain tax issue may require certain judgments. A descripïŋ―on of our accounïŋ―ng policies associated with tax related conïŋ―ngencies assumed as a part of a business combinaïŋ―on is provided under âBusiness Combinaïŋ―onsâ above. 

For those tax related conïŋ―ngencies that are not a part of a business combinaïŋ―on, we account for these uncertain tax issues pursuant to ASC 740, _Income Taxes_ , which contains a two-step approach to recognizing and measuring uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. The first step is to determine if the weight of available evidence indicates that it is more likely than not that the tax posiïŋ―on will be sustained in an audit, including resoluïŋ―on of any related appeals or liïŋ―gaïŋ―on processes. The second step is to measure the tax benefit as the largest amount that is more than 50% likely to be realized upon ulïŋ―mate seïŋ―lement. Although we believe that we have adequately reserved for our uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons, no assurance can be given with respect to the final outcome of these maïŋ―ers. We adjust reserves for our uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons due to changing facts and circumstances, such as the closing of a tax audit, judicial rulings, and refinement of esïŋ―mates or realizaïŋ―on of earnings or deducïŋ―ons that differ from our esïŋ―mates. To the extent that the final outcome of these maïŋ―ers is different than the amounts recorded, such differences generally will impact our provision for income taxes in the period in which such a determinaïŋ―on is made. Our provisions for income taxes include the impact of reserve provisions and changes to reserves that are considered appropriate and also include the related interest and penalïŋ―es.

## **Constant Currency Presentaïŋ―on** 

Our internaïŋ―onal operaïŋ―ons have provided and are expected to conïŋ―nue to provide a significant porïŋ―on of each of our businessesâ revenues and expenses. As a result, each of our businessesâ revenues and expenses and our total revenues and expenses will conïŋ―nue to be affected by changes in the U.S. Dollar against major internaïŋ―onal currencies. In order to provide a framework for assessing how our underlying businesses performed, excluding the effects of foreign currency rate fluctuaïŋ―ons, we compare the percent change in the results from one period to another period in this Annual Report using constant currency disclosure. To present this informaïŋ―on, current and comparaïŋ―ve prior period results for enïŋ―ïŋ―es reporïŋ―ng in currencies other than U.S. Dollars are converted into U.S. Dollars at constant exchange rates (i.e., the rates in effect on May 31, 2021, which was the last day of our prior fiscal year) rather than the actual exchange rates in effect during the respecïŋ―ve periods. For example, if an enïŋ―ty reporïŋ―ng in Euros had revenues of 1.0 million Euros from products sold on May 31, 2022 and 2021, our financial statements would reflect reported revenues of $1.07 million in fiscal 2022 (using 1.07 as the month-end average exchange rate for the period) and $1.22 million in fiscal 2021 (using 1.22 as the month-end average exchange rate for the period). The constant currency presentaïŋ―on, however, would translate the fiscal 2022 results using the fiscal 2021 exchange rate and indicate, in this example, no change in revenues during the period. In each of the tables below, we present the percent change based on actual, unrounded results in reported currency and in constant currency.

## **Cloud and License Business** 

Our cloud and license business engages in the sale and markeïŋ―ng of our applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies that are delivered through various deployment models and include: Oracle license support offerings; Oracle Cloud Services offerings; and Oracle cloud license and on-premise license offerings. License support revenues are typically generated through the sale of applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure license support contracts related to cloud licenses and on-premise licenses; are purchased by our customers at their opïŋ―on; and are generally recognized as revenues ratably over the contractual term, which is generally one year. Our cloud services deliver applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies on a subscripïŋ―on basis via cloud-based deployment models that we develop, provide unspecified updates and enhancements for, deploy, host, manage and support. Revenues for our cloud services are generally recognized over the contractual term, which is generally one to three years, or in the case of usage model contracts, as the cloud services are consumed. Cloud license and on-premise license revenues represent fees earned from granïŋ―ng customers licenses, generally on a perpetual basis, to use our database and middleware and our applicaïŋ―ons soïŋ―ware products within cloud and on-premise IT environments and are generally recognized up front at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the customer to download and use. We conïŋ―nue to place significant emphasis, both domesïŋ―cally and internaïŋ―onally, on direct sales through our own sales force. We also conïŋ―nue to market certain of our offerings through indirect channels. Costs associated with our cloud and license business are included in cloud services and license support expenses, and sales and markeïŋ―ng expenses. These costs are largely personnel and infrastructure related including the cost of providing our cloud services and license support offerings, salaries and commissions earned by our sales force for the sale of our cloud and license offerings, and markeïŋ―ng program costs.

## **Hardware Business** 

Our hardware businessâ revenues are generated from the sales of our Oracle Engineered Systems, server, storage, and industry-specific hardware offerings. The hardware product and related soïŋ―ware, such as an operaïŋ―ng system or firmware, are highly interdependent and interrelated and are accounted for as a combined performance obligaïŋ―on. The revenues for this combined performance obligaïŋ―on are generally recognized at the point in ïŋ―me that the hardware product is delivered to the customer and ownership is transferred to the customer. Our hardware business also earns revenues from the sale of hardware support contracts purchased by our customers at their opïŋ―on and that are generally recognized as revenues ratably as the hardware support services are delivered over the contractual term, which is generally one year. The majority of our hardware products are sold through indirect channels such as independent distributors and value-added resellers and we also market and sell our hardware products through our direct sales force. Operaïŋ―ng expenses associated with our hardware business include the cost of hardware products, which consists of expenses for materials and labor used to produce these products by our internal manufacturing operaïŋ―ons or by third-party manufacturers, warranty and related expenses and the impact of periodic changes in inventory valuaïŋ―on, including the impact of inventory determined to be excess and obsolete; the cost of materials used to repair customer products with eligible support contracts; the cost of labor and infrastructure to provide support services; and sales and markeïŋ―ng expenses, which are largely personnel related and include variable compensaïŋ―on earned by our sales force for the sales of our hardware offerings.

_**Working capital**_ **:** The decrease in working capital as of May 31, 2022 in comparison to May 31, 2021 was primarily due to $16.2 billion of cash used for repurchases of our common stock, $4.7 billion of cash paid for certain liïŋ―gaïŋ―on related charges that we generally do not expect to recur, $3.8 billion of longterm senior notes that were reclassified to current liabiliïŋ―es, cash used to pay dividends to our stockholders and cash used for capital expenditures during fiscal 2022. These unfavorable impacts were parïŋ―ally offset by the favorable impacts to our net current assets resulïŋ―ng from our net income, net cash proceeds of $318 million associated with the sale of certain operaïŋ―ng assets, and cash proceeds from stock opïŋ―on exercises, all of which occurred during fiscal 2022. ## **Stock-Based Awards** 

Our stock-based compensaïŋ―on program is a key component of the compensaïŋ―on package we provide to aïŋ―ract and retain certain of our talented employees and align their interests with the interests of exisïŋ―ng stockholders. 

We recognize that stock-based awards dilute exisïŋ―ng stockholders and have sought to control the number of stock-based awards granted while providing compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve compensaïŋ―on packages. Consistent with these dual goals, our cumulaïŋ―ve potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on since June 1, 2019 has been a weighted-average annualized rate of 1.3% per year. The potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on percentage is calculated as the average annualized new stock-based awards granted and assumed, net of stock-based awards forfeited by employees leaving the company, divided by the weighted-average outstanding shares during the calculaïŋ―on period. This maximum potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on will only result if all stock-based awards vest and, if applicable, are exercised. Of the outstanding stock opïŋ―ons at May 31, 2022, which generally have a ten-year exercise period, all have exercise prices lower than the market price of our common stock on such date. In recent years, our stock repurchase program has more than offset the diluïŋ―ve effect of our stock-based compensaïŋ―on program. However, we may modify the levels of our stock repurchases in the future depending on a number of factors, including the amount of cash we have available for acquisiïŋ―ons, to pay dividends, to repay or repurchase indebtedness or for other purposes. As of May 31, 2022, the maximum potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on from all outstanding stock-based awards, regardless of when granted and regardless of whether vested or unvested, was 8.4%. 

During fiscal 2022, the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board of Directors reviewed and approved the annual organizaïŋ―on-wide stock-based award grants to selected employees; all stock-based award grants to senior officers; and any individual grant of restricted stock units of 62,500 or greater. Each member of a separate execuïŋ―ve officer commiïŋ―ee, referred to as the Plan Commiïŋ―ee, was allocated a fiscal 2022 equity budget that could be used throughout the fiscal year to grant equity within his or her organizaïŋ―on, subject to certain limitaïŋ―ons established by the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee.

## **Item 7A.Quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve and Qualitaïŋ―ve Disclosures About Market Risk** 

## **Equity Price Risk** 

## **Marketable and Non-Marketable Equity Investments** 

Our marketable and non-marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments totaled $1.1 billion and $946 million as of May 31, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely. Our marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments in publicly traded companies are recorded at fair value, which is subject to market price volaïŋ―lity. Our nonmarketable equity securiïŋ―es investments in private companies not accounted for under the equity method are adjusted to fair value for observable transacïŋ―ons for idenïŋ―cal or similar investments of the same issuer or for impairment. Our non-marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments accounted for under the equity method, primarily in a related party enïŋ―ty, generally do not fluctuate based on market price changes. However, these equity method investments could be impaired if the carrying value exceeds the fair value and is not expected to recover. The ïŋ―ming and amounts of changes in fair value, if any, of our marketable and non-marketable equity investments depends on factors beyond our control, including the perceived and actual performance of the companies in which we invest. For addiïŋ―onal disclosure regarding the impact to our quarterly results of operaïŋ―ons from investment volaïŋ―lity, please refer to Item 1A Risk Factors included elsewhere in this Annual Report. 

## **Currency Risk** 

## **Foreign Currency Translaïŋ―on Risk** 

As described under âConstant Currency Presentaïŋ―onâ above, our internaïŋ―onal operaïŋ―ons have provided and are expected to conïŋ―nue to provide a significant porïŋ―on of our consolidated revenues and expenses that we report in U.S. Dollars. As a result, our consolidated revenues and expenses are affected and will conïŋ―nue to be affected by changes in the U.S. Dollar against major foreign currencies. Fluctuaïŋ―ons in foreign currencies impact the amount of total assets, liabiliïŋ―es, earnings and cash flows that we report for our foreign subsidiaries upon the translaïŋ―on of these amounts into U.S. Dollars for, and as of the end of, each reporïŋ―ng period. In parïŋ―cular, the strengthening of 

57

the U.S. Dollar generally will reduce the reported amount of our foreign-denominated cash, cash equivalents, marketable securiïŋ―es, total revenues and total expenses that we translate into U.S. Dollars and report in our consolidated financial statements for, and as of the end of, each reporïŋ―ng period. 

## **Foreign Currency Transacïŋ―on Risk** 

We transact business in various foreign currencies. Our principal currency exposures include the Euro, Japanese Yen, Saudi Arabian Riyal, Indian Rupee and Briïŋ―sh Pound. Our foreign currency exposures primarily arise from various intercompany transacïŋ―ons. We have established a program that primarily uïŋ―lizes foreign currency forward contracts to offset the risks that arise from the aforemenïŋ―oned transacïŋ―ons. Under this program, our strategy is to enter into foreign currency forward contracts for major currencies in which we have an exposure so that increases or decreases in our foreign currency exposures are offset by gains or losses on the foreign currency forward contracts which miïŋ―gate the risks and volaïŋ―lity associated with our foreign currency transacïŋ―ons. We may suspend this program from ïŋ―me to ïŋ―me. Our foreign currency forward contracts are generally short-term in duraïŋ―on and we do not use them for trading purposes. 

We realize gains or losses with respect to our foreign currency exposures, net of gains or losses from our foreign currency forward contracts, and we also incur costs to enter into these foreign currency forward contracts, substanïŋ―ally all of which are included in non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net in our consolidated financial statements. Our ulïŋ―mate realized gain or loss with respect to foreign currency exposures will generally depend on the size and type of cross-currency transacïŋ―ons that we enter into, the currency exchange rates associated with these exposures and changes in those rates, the net realized gain or loss on our foreign currency forward contracts and other factors. Furthermore, as a large porïŋ―on of our consolidated operaïŋ―ons are internaïŋ―onal, we could experience addiïŋ―onal foreign currency volaïŋ―lity in the future, in which the amounts and ïŋ―ming are unknown. Refer to Note 1 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements included elsewhere in this Annual Report for addiïŋ―onal details about our foreign currency forward contracts.

## **Item 9A.Controls and Procedures** 

## **Evaluaïŋ―on of Disclosure Controls and Procedures** 

As of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K, we carried out an evaluaïŋ―on under the supervision and with the parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on of our Disclosure Commiïŋ―ee and our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer, of the effecïŋ―veness of the design and operaïŋ―on of our disclosure controls and procedures pursuant to Exchange Act Rules 13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e). 

Based on our managementâs evaluaïŋ―on (with the parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on of our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer), as of the end of the period covered by this report, our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer has concluded that our disclosure controls and procedures were effecïŋ―ve as of May 31, 2022 to provide reasonable assurance that informaïŋ―on required to be disclosed by us in reports that we file or submit under the Exchange Act is (i) recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the ïŋ―me periods specified in the SEC rules and forms and (ii) accumulated and communicated to our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer as appropriate to allow ïŋ―mely decisions regarding required disclosure. 

## **Managementâs Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

Our management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng, as such term is defined in Exchange Act Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f). Under the supervision and with the parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on of our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer, we conducted an evaluaïŋ―on of the effecïŋ―veness of our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2022 based on the guidelines established in _Internal ControlâIntegrated Framework_ issued by the Commiïŋ―ee of Sponsoring Organizaïŋ―ons of the Treadway Commissionâs 2013 framework. Our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng includes policies and procedures that provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporïŋ―ng and the preparaïŋ―on of financial statements for external reporïŋ―ng purposes in accordance with U.S. GAAP. 

Based on the results of our evaluaïŋ―on, our management concluded that our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng was effecïŋ―ve as of May 31, 2022. We reviewed the results of managementâs assessment with our Finance and Audit Commiïŋ―ee. 

The effecïŋ―veness of our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2022 has been audited by Ernst & Young LLP, an independent registered public accounïŋ―ng firm, as stated in their report which is included in Part IV, Item 15 of this Annual Report. 

## **Changes in Internal Control over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

There were no changes in our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng idenïŋ―fied in connecïŋ―on with the evaluaïŋ―on required by paragraph (d) of Exchange Act Rules 13a-15 or 15d-15 that occurred during our last fiscal quarter that have materially affected, or are reasonably likely to materially affect, our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng. 

## **Inherent Limitaïŋ―ons on Effecïŋ―veness of Controls** 

Our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer, believes that our disclosure controls and procedures and internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng are designed to provide reasonable assurance of achieving their objecïŋ―ves and are effecïŋ―ve at the reasonable assurance level. However, our management does not expect that our disclosure controls and procedures or our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng will prevent all errors and all fraud. A control system, no maïŋ―er how well conceived and operated, can provide only reasonable, not absolute, assurance that the objecïŋ―ves of the control system are met. Further, the design of a control system must reflect the fact that there are resource constraints and the benefits of controls must be considered relaïŋ―ve to their costs. Because of the inherent limitaïŋ―ons in all control systems, no evaluaïŋ―on of controls can provide absolute assurance that all control issues and instances of fraud, if any, have been detected. These inherent limitaïŋ―ons include the realiïŋ―es that judgments in decision-making can be faulty and that breakdowns can occur because of a simple error or mistake. Addiïŋ―onally, controls can be circumvented by the individual acts of some persons, by collusion of two or more people or by management override of the controls. The design of any system of controls 

59 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

also is based in part upon certain assumpïŋ―ons about the likelihood of future events and there can be no assurance that any design will succeed in achieving its stated goals under all potenïŋ―al future condiïŋ―ons; over ïŋ―me, controls may become inadequate because of changes in condiïŋ―ons, or the degree of compliance with policies or procedures may deteriorate. Because of the inherent limitaïŋ―ons in a cost-effecïŋ―ve control system, misstatements due to error or fraud may occur and not be detected.

## **Report of Independent Registered Public Accounïŋ―ng Firm** 

To the Stockholders and the Board of Directors of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on 

## **Opinion on the Financial Statements** 

We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on (the Company) as of May 31, 2022 and 2021, the related consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons, comprehensive income, equity, and cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended May 31, 2022, and the related notes (collecïŋ―vely referred to as the âfinancial statementsâ). In our opinion, the financial statements present fairly, in all material respects, the financial posiïŋ―on of the Company at May 31, 2022 and 2021, and the results of its operaïŋ―ons and its cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended May 31, 2022, in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles. 

We also have audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounïŋ―ng Oversight Board (United States) (PCAOB), the Company's internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2022, based on criteria established in Internal Control-Integrated Framework issued by the Commiïŋ―ee of Sponsoring Organizaïŋ―ons of the Treadway Commission (2013 framework) and our report dated June 21, 2022 expressed an unqualified opinion thereon. 

## **Basis for Opinion** 

These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on the Companyâs financial statements based on our audits. We are a public accounïŋ―ng firm registered with the PCAOB and are required to be independent with respect to the Company in accordance with the U.S. federal securiïŋ―es laws and the applicable rules and regulaïŋ―ons of the Securiïŋ―es and Exchange Commission and the PCAOB. 

We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the PCAOB. Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement, whether due to error or fraud. Our audits included performing procedures to assess the risks of material misstatement of the financial statements, whether due to error or fraud, and performing procedures that respond to those risks. Such procedures included examining, on a test basis, evidence regarding the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements. Our audits also included evaluaïŋ―ng the accounïŋ―ng principles used and significant esïŋ―mates made by management, as well as evaluaïŋ―ng the overall presentaïŋ―on of the financial statements. We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion. 

## **Criïŋ―cal Audit Maïŋ―er** 

The criïŋ―cal audit maïŋ―er communicated below is a maïŋ―er arising from the current period audit of the financial statements that was communicated or required to be communicated to the audit commiïŋ―ee and that: (1) relates to accounts or disclosures that are material to the financial statements and (2) involved our especially challenging, subjecïŋ―ve, or complex judgments. The communicaïŋ―on of the criïŋ―cal audit maïŋ―er does not alter in any way our opinion on the financial statements, taken as a whole, and we are not, by communicaïŋ―ng the criïŋ―cal audit maïŋ―er below, providing a separate opinion on the criïŋ―cal audit maïŋ―er or on the accounts or disclosures to which it relates. 

_**Income Tax â Uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons**_ 

_Descripïŋ―on of the_ As discussed in Note 13 of the financial statements, the Company recognizes uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons and measures unrecognized tax _maïŋ―er_ benefits related to various domesïŋ―c and foreign maïŋ―ers. As of May 31, 2022, the total amount of unrecognized tax benefits was $7.3 billion, of which $4.3 billion, if recognized would impact the Companyâs effecïŋ―ve tax rate. The Company uses significant judgment in the accounïŋ―ng for uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons including the interpretaïŋ―on and applicaïŋ―on of tax laws and legal rulings in various jurisdicïŋ―ons. 

Audiïŋ―ng managementâs evaluaïŋ―on of whether an uncertain tax posiïŋ―on is more likely than not to be sustained and the measurement of the benefit of various tax posiïŋ―ons was complex, involved significant judgment, and was based on interpretaïŋ―ons and applicaïŋ―on of tax laws and legal rulings.

## **Report of Independent Registered Public Accounïŋ―ng Firm** 

To the Stockholders and the Board of Directors of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on 

## **Opinion on Internal Control Over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

We have audited Oracle Corporaïŋ―onâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2022, based on criteria established in Internal Control â Integrated Framework issued by the Commiïŋ―ee of Sponsoring Organizaïŋ―ons of the Treadway Commission (2013 framework) (the COSO criteria). In our opinion, Oracle Corporaïŋ―on (the Company) maintained, in all material respects, effecïŋ―ve internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2022, based on the COSO criteria. 

We also have audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounïŋ―ng Oversight Board (United States) (PCAOB), the consolidated balance sheets of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on as of May 31, 2022 and 2021, the related consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons, comprehensive income, equity, and cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended May 31, 2022, and the related notes and our report dated June 21, 2022 expressed an unqualified opinion thereon. 

## **Basis for Opinion** 

The Companyâs management is responsible for maintaining effecïŋ―ve internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng and for its assessment of the effecïŋ―veness of internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng included in the accompanying Managementâs Report on Internal Control Over Financial Reporïŋ―ng. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on the Companyâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng based on our audit. We are a public accounïŋ―ng firm registered with the PCAOB and are required to be independent with respect to the Company in accordance with the U.S. federal securiïŋ―es laws and the applicable rules and regulaïŋ―ons of the Securiïŋ―es and Exchange Commission and the PCAOB. 

We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the PCAOB. Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether effecïŋ―ve internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng was maintained in all material respects. 

Our audit included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists, tesïŋ―ng and evaluaïŋ―ng the design and operaïŋ―ng effecïŋ―veness of internal control based on the assessed risk, and performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis for our opinion. 

## **Definiïŋ―on and Limitaïŋ―ons of Internal Control Over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

A companyâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporïŋ―ng and the preparaïŋ―on of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles. A companyâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng includes those policies and procedures that (1) pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transacïŋ―ons and disposiïŋ―ons of the assets of the company; (2) provide reasonable assurance that transacïŋ―ons are recorded as necessary to permit preparaïŋ―on of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles, and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizaïŋ―ons of management and directors of the company; and (3) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevenïŋ―on or ïŋ―mely detecïŋ―on of unauthorized acquisiïŋ―on, use, or disposiïŋ―on of the companyâs assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements. 

Because of its inherent limitaïŋ―ons, internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng may not prevent or detect misstatements. Also, projecïŋ―ons of any evaluaïŋ―on of effecïŋ―veness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in condiïŋ―ons, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.

## **1. ORGANIZATION AND SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES** 

Oracle Corporaïŋ―on provides products and services that substanïŋ―ally address all aspects of enterprise informaïŋ―on technology (IT) environments, including applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. We deliver our products and services to customers worldwide through a variety of flexible and interoperable IT deployment models, including cloud-based, Cloud@Customer (an instance of Oracle Cloud in the customerâs own data center), on-premise and hybrid models. Oracle Cloud Soïŋ―ware-as-a-Service and Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (SaaS and OCI, respecïŋ―vely, and collecïŋ―vely, Oracle Cloud Services) offerings provide a comprehensive and integrated stack of applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure services delivered via cloud-based deployment models that Oracle develops, deploys, hosts, upgrades, supports and manages for the customer. Customers may also elect to purchase Oracle soïŋ―ware licenses and hardware products and related services to manage their own cloud-based or on-premise IT environments. Customers that purchase our soïŋ―ware licenses may elect to purchase license support contracts, which provide our customers with rights to unspecified license upgrades and maintenance releases issued during the support period as well as technical support assistance. Customers that purchase our hardware products may elect to purchase hardware support contracts, which provide customers with soïŋ―ware updates and can include product repairs, maintenance services, and technical support services. We also offer customers a broad set of services offerings that are designed to improve customer uïŋ―lizaïŋ―on of their investments in Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. 

Oracle Corporaïŋ―on conducts business globally and was incorporated in 2005 as a Delaware corporaïŋ―on and is the successor to operaïŋ―ons originally begun in June 1977. 

## **Basis of Financial Statements** 

The consolidated financial statements included our accounts and the accounts of our wholly- and majority-owned subsidiaries. Noncontrolling interest posiïŋ―ons of certain of our consolidated enïŋ―ïŋ―es are reported as a separate component of consolidated equity from the equity aïŋ―ributable to Oracleâs stockholders for all periods presented. The noncontrolling interests in our net income were not significant to our consolidated results for the periods presented and therefore have not been presented separately and instead are included as a component of non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. Intercompany transacïŋ―ons and balances have been eliminated. 

The comparability of our consolidated financial statements as of and for the year ended May 31, 2022 was impacted by $4.7 billion of certain liïŋ―gaïŋ―on related charges that are more fully described in Note 16 below. The comparability of our consolidated financial statements for the year ended May 31, 2021 was impacted by a $2.3 billion net income tax benefit related to the parïŋ―al realignment of our legal enïŋ―ty structure that resulted in the intra-group transfer of certain intellectual property rights. Refer to Note 13 below for addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on regarding our income taxes. 

In fiscal 2022, we adopted Accounïŋ―ng Standards Update (ASU) 2019-12, _Income Taxes (Topic 740): Simplifying the Accounïŋ―ng for Income Taxes; and_ ASU 2021-08, _Business Combinaïŋ―ons (Topic 805): Accounïŋ―ng for Contract Assets and Contract Liabiliïŋ―es from Contracts with Customers_ , neither of which had a material impact to our consolidated financial statements for the year ended May 31, 2022.

These accounïŋ―ng principles require us to make certain esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons. We believe that the esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons upon which we rely are reasonable based upon

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on** 

Our sources of revenues include: 

- cloud and license revenues, which include the sale of: cloud services and license support; and cloud licenses and on-premise licenses, which typically represent perpetual soïŋ―ware licenses purchased by customers for use in both cloud and on-premise IT environments; 

- hardware revenues, which include the sale of hardware products, including Oracle Engineered Systems, servers, and storage products, and industry-specific hardware; and hardware support revenues; and 

- services revenues, which are earned from providing cloud-, license- and hardware-related services including consulïŋ―ng and advanced customer services. 

License support revenues are typically generated through the sale of license support contracts related to cloud license and on-premise licenses purchased by our customers at their opïŋ―on. License support contracts provide customers with rights to unspecified soïŋ―ware product upgrades, maintenance releases and patches released during the term of the support period and include internet access to technical content, as well as internet and telephone access to technical support personnel. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net cloud license and on-premise license fees. Substanïŋ―ally all of our customers elect to purchase and renew their license support contracts annually. 

Cloud services revenues include revenues from Oracle Cloud Services offerings, which deliver applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies via cloud-based deployment models that we develop funcïŋ―onality for, provide unspecified updates and enhancements for, deploy, host, manage, upgrade and support and that customers access by entering into a subscripïŋ―on agreement with us for a stated period. 

Cloud license and on-premise license revenues primarily represent amounts earned from granïŋ―ng customers perpetual licenses to use our database, middleware, applicaïŋ―on and industry-specific soïŋ―ware products, which our customers use for cloud-based, on-premise and other IT environments. The vast majority of our cloud license and on-premise license arrangements include license support contracts, which are entered into at the customerâs opïŋ―on. 

Revenues from the sale of hardware products represent amounts earned primarily from the sale of our Oracle Engineered Systems, computer servers, storage, and industry-specific hardware. Our hardware support offerings generally provide customers with soïŋ―ware updates for the soïŋ―ware components that are essenïŋ―al to the funcïŋ―onality of the hardware products purchased and can also include product repairs, maintenance services and technical support services. Hardware support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net hardware products fees. 

Our services are offered to customers as standalone arrangements or as a part of arrangements to customers buying other products and services. Our consulïŋ―ng services are designed to help our customers to, among others, deploy, architect, integrate, upgrade and secure their investments in Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. Our advanced customer services are designed to provide supplemental support services, performance services and higher availability for Oracle products and services.

We apply the provisions of ASC 606, _Revenue From Contracts with Customers_ (ASC 606) as a single standard for revenue recogniïŋ―on that applies to all of our cloud, license, hardware and services arrangements and generally require revenues to be recognized upon the transfer of control of promised goods or services provided to our customers, reflecïŋ―ng the amount of consideraïŋ―on we expect to receive for those goods or services. Pursuant to ASC 606, revenues are recognized upon the applicaïŋ―on of the following steps: 

- idenïŋ―ficaïŋ―on of the contract, or contracts, with a customer; 

- idenïŋ―ficaïŋ―on of the performance obligaïŋ―ons in the contract; 

- determinaïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price; 

- allocaïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price to each performance obligaïŋ―on in the contract; and 

- recogniïŋ―on of revenues when, or as, the contractual performance obligaïŋ―ons are saïŋ―sfied. 

Our customers that contract with us for the provision of cloud services, soïŋ―ware, hardware or other services include businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and our channel partners, which include resellers and system integrators. 

The ïŋ―ming of revenue recogniïŋ―on may differ from the ïŋ―ming of invoicing to our customers. We record an unbilled receivable, which is included within accounts receivable on our consolidated balance sheets, when revenue is recognized prior to invoicing. We record deferred revenues on our consolidated balance sheets when revenues are to be recognized subsequent to cash collecïŋ―on for an invoice. Our standard payment terms are generally net 30 days but may vary. Invoices for cloud license and on-premise licenses and hardware products are generally issued when the license is made available for customer use or upon delivery to the customer of the hardware product. Invoices for license support and hardware support contracts are generally invoiced annually in advance. Cloud SaaS and cloud infrastructure contracts are generally invoiced annually, quarterly or monthly in advance. Services are generally invoiced in advance or as the services are performed. Most contracts that contain a financing component are contracts financed through our Oracle financing division. The transacïŋ―on price for a contract that is financed through our Oracle financing division is adjusted to reflect the ïŋ―me value of money and interest revenue is recorded as a component of non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net within our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons based on market rates in the country in which the transacïŋ―on is being financed. 

Our revenue arrangements generally include standard warranty or service level provisions that our arrangements will perform and operate in all material respects as defined in the respecïŋ―ve agreements, the financial impacts of which have historically been and are expected to conïŋ―nue to be insignificant. Our arrangements generally do not include a general right of return relaïŋ―ve to the delivered products or services. We recognize revenues net of any taxes collected from customers, which are subsequently remiïŋ―ed to governmental authoriïŋ―es. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Cloud Services** 

Revenues from cloud services provided on a subscripïŋ―on basis are generally recognized ratably over the contractual period that the cloud services are delivered, beginning on the date our service is made available to a customer. We recognize revenue ratably because the customer receives and consumes the benefits of the cloud services throughout the contract period. Revenues from cloud services that are provided on a consumpïŋ―on basis, such as metered services, are generally recognized based on the uïŋ―lizaïŋ―on of the services by the customer. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for License Support and Hardware Support** 

Oracleâs primary performance obligaïŋ―ons with respect to license support contracts and hardware support contracts are to provide customers with technical support as needed and unspecified soïŋ―ware product upgrades, maintenance releases and patches during the term of the support period, if and when they are available, and hardware product repairs, as applicable. Oracle is obligated to make the license and hardware support services
