## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Cloud Licenses and On-Premise Licenses** 

Revenues from disïŋ―nct cloud license and on-premise license performance obligaïŋ―ons are generally recognized upfront at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the customer to download and use. Revenues from usage-based royalty arrangements for disïŋ―nct cloud licenses and on-premise licenses are recognized at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware end user usage occurs. For usage-based royalty arrangements with a fixed minimum guarantee amount, the minimum amount is generally recognized upfront when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the royalty customer. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Hardware Products** 

The hardware product and related soïŋ―ware, such as an operaïŋ―ng system or firmware, are highly interdependent and interrelated and are accounted for as a combined performance obligaïŋ―on. The revenues for this combined performance obligaïŋ―on are generally recognized at the point in ïŋ―me that the hardware product is delivered and ownership is transferred to the customer. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Services** 

Services revenues are generally recognized over ïŋ―me as the services are performed. Revenues for fixed price services are generally recognized over ïŋ―me applying input methods to esïŋ―mate progress to compleïŋ―on. Revenues for consumpïŋ―on-based services are generally recognized as the services are performed. 

## **Allocaïŋ―on of the Transacïŋ―on Price for Contracts that have Mulïŋ―ple Performance Obligaïŋ―ons** 

Many of our contracts include mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons. Judgment is required in determining whether each performance obligaïŋ―on is disïŋ―nct. Oracle products and services generally do not require a significant amount of integraïŋ―on or interdependency; therefore, our products and services are generally not combined. We allocate the transacïŋ―on price for each contract to each performance obligaïŋ―on based on the relaïŋ―ve standalone selling price (SSP) for each performance obligaïŋ―on within each contract. 

We use judgment in determining the SSP for products and services. For substanïŋ―ally all performance obligaïŋ―ons except cloud licenses and on-premise licenses, we are able to establish the SSP based on the observable prices of products or services sold separately in comparable circumstances to similar customers. We typically establish an SSP range for our products and services which is reassessed on a periodic basis or when facts and circumstances change. Our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses have not historically been sold on a standalone basis, as the vast majority of all customers elect to purchase license support contracts at the ïŋ―me of a cloud license and on-premise license purchase. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net fees paid by the customer to access the license. We are unable to establish the SSP for our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses based on observable prices given the same products are sold for a broad range of amounts (that is, the selling price is highly variable) and a representaïŋ―ve SSP is not discernible from past transacïŋ―ons or other observable evidence. As a result, the SSP for a cloud license and an on-premise license included in a contract with mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons is generally determined by applying a residual approach whereby all other performance obligaïŋ―ons within a contract are first allocated a porïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price based upon their respecïŋ―ve SSPs, with any residual amount of transacïŋ―on price allocated to cloud license and onpremise license revenues.

## **Remaining Performance Obligaïŋ―ons from Customer Contracts** 

Trade receivables, net of allowance for credit losses, and deferred revenues are reported net of related uncollected deferred revenues in our consolidated balance sheets as of May 31, 2022 and 2021. The amount of revenues recognized during the year ended May 31, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely, that were included in the opening deferred revenues balance as of May 31, 2021 and 2020, respecïŋ―vely, was approximately $8.8 billion and $8.0 billion, respecïŋ―vely. Revenues recognized from performance obligaïŋ―ons saïŋ―sfied in prior periods and impairment losses recognized on our receivables were immaterial during each year ended May 31, 2022, 2021 and 2020. 

Remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons represent contracted revenues that had not yet been recognized, and include deferred revenues; invoices that have been issued to customers but were uncollected and have not been recognized as revenues; and amounts that will be invoiced and recognized as revenues in future periods. The volumes and amounts of customer contracts that we book and total revenues that we recognize are impacted by a variety of seasonal factors. In each fiscal year, the amounts and volumes of contracïŋ―ng acïŋ―vity and our total revenues are typically highest in our fourth fiscal quarter and lowest in our first fiscal quarter. These seasonal impacts influence how our remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons change over ïŋ―me and, combined with foreign exchange rate fluctuaïŋ―ons and other factors, influence the amount of remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons that we report at a point in ïŋ―me. As of May 31, 2022, our remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons were $46.6 billion, approximately 57% of which we expect to recognize as revenues over the next twelve months, 32% over the subsequent month 13 to month 36, and the remainder thereaïŋ―er. 

## **Sales of Financing Receivables** 

We offer certain of our customers the opïŋ―on to acquire certain of our cloud and license, hardware and services offerings through separate long-term payment contracts. We generally sell these contracts that we have financed for our customers on a non-recourse basis to financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons within 90 days of the contractsâ dates of execuïŋ―on. We record the transfers of amounts due from customers to financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons as sales of financing receivables because we are considered to have surrendered control of these financing receivables. During fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020, $1.8 billion, $1.7 billion and $1.5 billion, respecïŋ―vely, of our financing receivables were sold to financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons. 

## **Business Combinaïŋ―ons** 

We apply the provisions of ASC 805, _Business Combinaïŋ―ons_ (ASC 805), in accounïŋ―ng for our acquisiïŋ―ons. ASC 805 requires that we evaluate whether a transacïŋ―on pertains to an acquisiïŋ―on of assets, or to an acquisiïŋ―on of a business. A business is defined as an integrated set of assets and acïŋ―viïŋ―es that is capable of being conducted and managed for the purpose of providing a return to investors. Asset acquisiïŋ―ons are accounted for by allocaïŋ―ng the cost of the acquisiïŋ―on to the individual assets and liabiliïŋ―es assumed on a relaïŋ―ve fair value basis; whereas the acquisiïŋ―on of a business requires us to recognize separately from goodwill the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values. Goodwill as of the business acquisiïŋ―on date is measured as the excess of consideraïŋ―on transferred over the net of the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values of the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed. While we use our best esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons to accurately value assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the business acquisiïŋ―on date as well as any conïŋ―ngent consideraïŋ―on, where applicable, our esïŋ―mates are inherently uncertain and subject to refinement. As a result, during the measurement period, which may be up to one year from the business acquisiïŋ―on date, we record adjustments to the assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed with the corresponding offset to goodwill. Upon the conclusion of a business acquisiïŋ―onâs measurement period or final determinaïŋ―on of the values of assets acquired or liabiliïŋ―es assumed, whichever comes first, any subsequent adjustments are recorded to our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. Costs to exit or restructure certain acïŋ―viïŋ―es of an acquired company or our internal operaïŋ―ons are accounted for as terminaïŋ―on and exit costs pursuant to ASC 420, _Exit or Disposal Cost Obligaïŋ―ons_ , and are accounted for separately from the business

## **Marketable and Non-Marketable Investments** 

In accordance with ASC 320, _InvestmentsâDebt Securiïŋ―es_ , and based on our intenïŋ―ons regarding these instruments, we classify substanïŋ―ally all of our marketable debt securiïŋ―es investments as available-for-sale. We periodically evaluate our investments to determine if impairment charges are required. Substanïŋ―ally all of our marketable debt securiïŋ―es investments are classified as current based on the nature of the investments and their availability for use in current operaïŋ―ons. 

Investments in equity securiïŋ―es, other than any equity method investments, are generally recorded at their fair values, if the fair values are readily determinable. Non-marketable equity securiïŋ―es where we do not have control of, nor significant influence in, the investee are recorded at cost, less any impairment, adjusted for observable price changes from orderly transacïŋ―ons for idenïŋ―cal or similar investments of the same issuer with any gains or losses recorded as a component of non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net as of and for each reporïŋ―ng period. For investments through which we have significant influence in, but not control of, the investee, we account for such investments pursuant to the equity method of accounïŋ―ng whereby we record our proporïŋ―onate share of the investeeâs earnings or losses, amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on of differences between our investment basis and the proporïŋ―onal book equity of the investee, and impairment, if any, as a component of non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net for each reporïŋ―ng period.

## **Fair Values of Financial Instruments** 

We apply the provisions of ASC 820, _Fair Value Measurement_ (ASC 820), to our assets and liabiliïŋ―es that we are required to measure at fair value pursuant to other accounïŋ―ng standards, including our investments in marketable debt and equity securiïŋ―es and our derivaïŋ―ve financial instruments. 

The addiïŋ―onal disclosures regarding our fair value measurements are included in Note 4. 

## **Allowances for Credit Losses** 

We record allowances for credit losses based upon a specific review of all significant outstanding invoices. For those invoices not specifically reviewed, provisions are provided at differing rates, based upon the age of the receivable, the collecïŋ―on history associated with the geographic region that the receivable was recorded in and current and expected future economic condiïŋ―ons. We write-off a receivable and charge it against its recorded allowance when we have exhausted our collecïŋ―on efforts without success. 

## **Concentraïŋ―ons of Credit Risk** 

Financial instruments that are potenïŋ―ally subject to concentraïŋ―ons of credit risk consist primarily of cash and cash equivalents, marketable securiïŋ―es, derivaïŋ―ves and trade receivables. Our cash and cash equivalents are generally held with large, diverse financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons worldwide to reduce the amount of exposure to any single financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―on. Investment policies have been implemented that limit purchases of marketable debt securiïŋ―es to investmentgrade securiïŋ―es. Our derivaïŋ―ve contracts are transacted with various financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons with high credit standings and any exposure to counterparty creditrelated losses in these contracts is largely miïŋ―gated with collateral security agreements that provide for collateral to be received or posted when the net fair values of these contracts fluctuate from contractually established thresholds. We generally do not require collateral to secure accounts receivable. The risk with respect to trade receivables is miïŋ―gated by credit evaluaïŋ―ons we perform on our customers, the short duraïŋ―on of our payment terms for the significant majority of our customer contracts and by the diversificaïŋ―on of our customer base. No single customer accounted for 10% or more of our total revenues in fiscal 2022, 2021 or 2020. 

We outsource the manufacturing, assembly and delivery of the substanïŋ―al majority of our hardware products to a variety of companies, many of which are located outside the U.S. Further, we have simplified our supply chain processes by reducing the number of third-party manufacturing partners and the number of locaïŋ―ons where these third-party manufacturers build our hardware products. Any inability of these third-party manufacturing partners to deliver the contracted services for our hardware products could adversely impact future operaïŋ―ng results of our cloud and license and hardware businesses.

demand within specific ïŋ―me horizons (generally six to nine months). Inventories in excess of future demand are wriïŋ―en down and charged to hardware expenses. In addiïŋ―on, we assess the impact of changing technology to our inventories and we write down inventories that are considered obsolete. ## **Other Receivables** 

Other receivables represent value-added tax and sales tax receivables associated with the sale of our products and services to third parïŋ―es. Other receivables are included in prepaid expenses and other current assets in our consolidated balance sheets and totaled $791 million and $798 million at May 31, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely. 

## **Deferred Sales Commissions** 

We defer sales commissions earned by our sales force that are considered to be incremental and recoverable costs of obtaining a cloud, license support and hardware support contract. Iniïŋ―al sales commissions for the majority of these aforemenïŋ―oned contracts are generally deferred and amorïŋ―zed on a straightline basis over a period of benefit that we esïŋ―mate to be four years. We determine the period of benefit by taking into consideraïŋ―on the historical and expected duraïŋ―ons of our customer contracts, the expected useful lives of our technologies, and other factors. Sales commissions for renewal contracts relaïŋ―ng to certain of our cloud-based arrangements are generally deferred and then amorïŋ―zed on a straight-line basis over the related contractual renewal period, which is generally one to three years. Amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on of deferred sales commissions is included as a component of sales and markeïŋ―ng expenses in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons and asset balances for deferred sales commissions are included in other current assets and other non-current assets in our consolidated balance sheets. 

## **Property, Plant and Equipment** 

Property, plant and equipment are stated at cost, less accumulated depreciaïŋ―on. Depreciaïŋ―on is computed using the straight-line method based on esïŋ―mated useful lives of the assets, which range from one to 40 years. Leasehold improvements are amorïŋ―zed over the lesser of the esïŋ―mated useful lives of the improvements or the lease terms, as appropriate. Property, plant and equipment are periodically reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable. We did not recognize any significant property impairment charges in fiscal 2022, 2021 or 2020. 

## **Goodwill, Intangible Assets and Impairment Assessments** 

Goodwill represents the excess of the purchase price in a business combinaïŋ―on over the fair value of net tangible and intangible assets acquired. Intangible assets that are not considered to have an indefinite useful life are itemized in Note 6 below and are amorïŋ―zed over their useful lives, which generally range from one to 10 years. Each period we evaluate the esïŋ―mated remaining useful lives of purchased intangible assets and whether events or changes in circumstances warrant a revision to the remaining periods of amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on. 

The carrying amounts of our goodwill and intangible assets are periodically reviewed for impairment (at least annually for goodwill and indefinite lived intangible assets) and whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying value of these assets may not be recoverable. When goodwill is assessed for impairment, we have the opïŋ―on to perform an assessment of qualitaïŋ―ve factors of impairment (opïŋ―onal assessment) prior to necessitaïŋ―ng a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve impairment test. Should the opïŋ―onal assessment be used for any given fiscal year, qualitaïŋ―ve factors considered for a reporïŋ―ng unit include: cost factors; financial performance; legal, regulatory, contractual, poliïŋ―cal, business, or other factors; enïŋ―ty specific factors; industry and market consideraïŋ―ons; macroeconomic condiïŋ―ons; and other relevant events and factors affecïŋ―ng the reporïŋ―ng unit. If we determine in

the qualitaïŋ―ve assessment that it is more likely than not that the fair value of the reporïŋ―ng unit is less than its carrying value, a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve test is then performed. Otherwise, no further tesïŋ―ng is required. For those reporïŋ―ng units tested using a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve approach, we compare the fair value of each reporïŋ―ng unit with the carrying amount of the reporïŋ―ng unit, including goodwill. To determine the fair value of each reporïŋ―ng unit we uïŋ―lize esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons including esïŋ―mated future cash flows the reporïŋ―ng unit is expected to generate on a discounted basis; the discount rate used as a part of the discounted cash flow analysis; future economic and market condiïŋ―ons; and market comparables of peer companies, among others. If, as per the quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve test, the esïŋ―mated fair value of the reporïŋ―ng unit is less than the carrying amount of the reporïŋ―ng unit, impairment is recognized for the difference, limited to the amount of goodwill recognized for the reporïŋ―ng unit. Our most recent goodwill impairment analysis was performed on March 1, 2022 and did not result in a goodwill impairment charge. We did not recognize impairment charges in fiscal 2021 or 2020. 

Recoverability of finite lived intangible assets is measured by comparison of the carrying amount of the asset to the future undiscounted cash flows that are expected to be generated by the lowest level associated asset grouping. Recoverability of indefinite lived intangible assets is measured by comparison of the carrying amount of the asset to its fair value. If the asset is considered to be impaired, the amount of any impairment is measured as the difference between the carrying value and the fair value of the impaired asset. We did not recognize any intangible asset impairment charges in fiscal 2022, 2021 or 2020. At least annually, we assess the useful lives of our finite lived intangible assets and may adjust the period over which these assets are amorïŋ―zed whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that a shorter amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on period is more reflecïŋ―ve of the period in which these assets contribute to our cash flows. 

## **Derivaïŋ―ve Financial Instruments** 

During fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020, we used derivaïŋ―ve financial instruments to manage foreign currency and interest rate risks. We do not use derivaïŋ―ve financial instruments for trading purposes. We account for these instruments in accordance with ASC 815, _Derivaïŋ―ves and Hedging_ (ASC 815), which requires that every derivaïŋ―ve instrument be recorded on the balance sheet as either an asset or liability measured at its fair value as of each reporïŋ―ng date. ASC 815 also requires that changes in our derivaïŋ―vesâ fair values be recognized in earnings, unless specific hedge accounïŋ―ng and documentaïŋ―on criteria are met (i.e., the instruments are accounted for as hedges). 

The accounïŋ―ng for changes in the fair value of a derivaïŋ―ve depends on the intended use of the derivaïŋ―ve and the resulïŋ―ng designaïŋ―on. For a derivaïŋ―ve instrument designated as a fair value hedge, loss or gain aïŋ―ributable to the risk being hedged is recognized in earnings in the period of change with a corresponding earnings offset recorded to the item for which the risk is being hedged. 

## **Leases** 

We determine if an arrangement is a lease at its incepïŋ―on. Operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es are recognized at the lease commencement date based on the present value of lease payments over the lease term. We generally use our incremental borrowing rate based on the informaïŋ―on available at the lease commencement date in determining the present value of future payments, because the implicit rate of the lease is generally not known. ROU assets related to our operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es are measured at lease incepïŋ―on based on the iniïŋ―al measurement of the lease liability, plus any prepaid lease payments and less any lease incenïŋ―ves. Our lease terms that are used in determining our operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es at lease incepïŋ―on may include opïŋ―ons to extend or terminate the leases when it is reasonably certain that we will exercise such opïŋ―ons. We amorïŋ―ze our ROU assets as operaïŋ―ng lease expense generally on a straight-line basis over the lease term and classify both the lease amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on and imputed interest as operaïŋ―ng expenses. We have lease agreements with lease and non-lease components, and in such cases, we generally account for the components as a single lease component. We do not recognize lease assets and lease liabiliïŋ―es for any lease with an original lease term of less than one year.

## **Foreign Currency** 

We transact business in various foreign currencies. In general, the funcïŋ―onal currency of a foreign operaïŋ―on is the local countryâs currency. Consequently, revenues and expenses of operaïŋ―ons outside the U.S. are translated into U.S. Dollars using weighted-average exchange rates while assets and liabiliïŋ―es of operaïŋ―ons outside the U.S. are translated into U.S. Dollars using exchange rates at the balance sheet dates. The effects of foreign currency translaïŋ―on adjustments are substanïŋ―ally included in stockholdersâ equity as a component of AOCL in the accompanying consolidated balance sheets and related periodic movements are summarized as a line item in our consolidated statements of comprehensive income. ## **Stock-Based Compensaïŋ―on** 

We account for share-based payments to employees, including grants of service-based restricted stock unit awards, service-based employee stock opïŋ―ons, performance-based stock opïŋ―ons (PSOs), and purchases under employee stock purchase plans in accordance with ASC 718, _Compensaïŋ―on_ â _Stock Compensaïŋ―on,_ which requires that share-based payments (to the extent they are compensatory) be recognized in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons based on their fair values. We account for forfeitures of stock-based awards as they occur. 

For our service-based stock awards, we recognize stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense on a straight-line basis over the service period of the award, which is generally four years. 

For our PSOs, we recognize stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense on a straight-line basis related to awards that are probable of achievement over the longer of the (a) esïŋ―mated implicit service period for performance-metric achievement, or (b) derived service period for market-based metric achievement. During our interim and annual reporïŋ―ng periods, stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense is recorded based on expected aïŋ―ainment of performance targets. Changes in our esïŋ―mates of the expected aïŋ―ainment of performance targets that result in a change in the number of shares that are expected to vest, or changes in our esïŋ―mates of implicit service periods, may cause the amount of stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense that we record for each interim reporïŋ―ng period to vary. Any changes in esïŋ―mates that impact our expectaïŋ―on of the number of shares that are expected to vest are reflected in the amount of stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense that we recognize for each PSO tranche on a cumulaïŋ―ve catch up basis during each interim reporïŋ―ng period in which such esïŋ―mates are altered. Changes in esïŋ―mates of the implicit service periods are recognized prospecïŋ―vely.

## **Income Taxes** 

We account for income taxes in accordance with ASC 740, _Income Taxes_ (ASC 740). Deferred income taxes are recorded for the expected tax consequences of temporary differences between the tax bases of assets and liabiliïŋ―es for financial reporïŋ―ng purposes and amounts recognized for income tax purposes. We record a valuaïŋ―on allowance to reduce our deferred tax assets to the amount of future tax benefit that is more likely than not to be realized. 

A two-step approach is applied pursuant to ASC 740 in the recogniïŋ―on and measurement of uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. The first step is to determine if the weight of available evidence indicates that it is more likely than not that the tax posiïŋ―on will be sustained in an audit, including resoluïŋ―on of any related appeals or liïŋ―gaïŋ―on processes. The second step is to measure the tax benefit as the largest amount that is more than 50% likely to be realized upon ulïŋ―mate seïŋ―lement. We recognize interest and penalïŋ―es related to uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons in our provision for income taxes line of our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. 

A descripïŋ―on of our accounïŋ―ng policies associated with tax related conïŋ―ngencies and valuaïŋ―on allowances assumed as a part of a business combinaïŋ―on is provided under âBusiness Combinaïŋ―onsâ above. 

## **Recent Accounïŋ―ng Pronouncements** 

**Financial Instruments:** In March 2020, the Financial Accounïŋ―ng Standards Board (FASB) issued ASU 2020-04, _Reference Rate Reform (Topic 848): Facilitaïŋ―on of the Effects of Reference Rate Reform on Financial Reporïŋ―ng_ (ASU 2020-04) and also issued subsequent amendments to the iniïŋ―al guidance (collecïŋ―vely, Topic 848). Topic 848 provides opïŋ―onal guidance for contract modificaïŋ―ons and certain hedging relaïŋ―onships associated with the transiïŋ―on from reference rates that are expected to be disconïŋ―nued. We will adopt Topic 848 when our relevant contracts are modified upon transiïŋ―on to alternaïŋ―ve reference rates and expect this to occur through December 31, 2022. We do not expect our adopïŋ―on of Topic 848 to have a material impact on our consolidated financial statements.

## **Acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner Corporaïŋ―on** 

On December 20, 2021, we entered into an Agreement and Plan of Merger (Merger Agreement) with Cerner Corporaïŋ―on (Cerner), a provider of digital informaïŋ―on systems used within hospitals and health systems that are designed to enable medical professionals to deliver beïŋ―er healthcare to individual païŋ―ents and communiïŋ―es. 

On January 19, 2022, pursuant to the Merger Agreement, we commenced a tender offer to purchase all of the issued and outstanding shares of common stock of Cerner at a purchase price of $95.00 per share, net to the seller in cash, without interest thereon, based upon the terms and subject to the condiïŋ―ons set forth in the Offer to Purchase dated January 19, 2022, and the related Leïŋ―er of Transmiïŋ―al.

## **4. FAIR VALUE MEASUREMENTS** 

We perform fair value measurements in accordance with ASC 820. ASC 820 defines fair value as the price that would be received from selling an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transacïŋ―on between market parïŋ―cipants at the measurement date. When determining the fair value measurements for assets and liabiliïŋ―es required to be recorded at their fair values, we consider the principal or most advantageous market in which we would transact and consider assumpïŋ―ons that market parïŋ―cipants would use when pricing the assets or liabiliïŋ―es, such as inherent risk, transfer restricïŋ―ons and risk of nonperformance. 

ASC 820 establishes a fair value hierarchy that requires an enïŋ―ty to maximize the use of observable inputs and minimize the use of unobservable inputs when measuring fair value. An assetâs or a liabilityâs categorizaïŋ―on within the fair value hierarchy is based upon the lowest level of input that is significant to the fair value measurement. ASC 820 establishes three levels of inputs that may be used to measure fair value: 

- Level 1: quoted prices in acïŋ―ve markets for idenïŋ―cal assets or liabiliïŋ―es; 

- Level 2: inputs other than Level 1 that are observable, either directly or indirectly, such as quoted prices in acïŋ―ve markets for similar assets or liabiliïŋ―es, quoted prices for idenïŋ―cal or similar assets or liabiliïŋ―es in markets that are not acïŋ―ve, or other inputs that are observable or can be corroborated by observable market data for substanïŋ―ally the full term of the assets or liabiliïŋ―es; or 

- Level 3: unobservable inputs that are supported by liïŋ―le or no market acïŋ―vity and that are significant to the fair values of the assets or liabiliïŋ―es.

Our valuaïŋ―on techniques used to measure the fair values of our instruments that were classified as Level 1 in the table above were derived from quoted market prices and acïŋ―ve markets for these instruments that exist. Our valuaïŋ―on techniques used to measure the fair values of Level 2 instruments listed in the table above were derived from the following: non-binding market consensus prices that were corroborated by observable market data, quoted market prices for similar instruments, or pricing models, such as discounted cash flow techniques, with all significant inputs derived from or corroborated by observable market data including reference rate yield curves, among others.

## **Senior Notes** 

Interest is payable semi-annually for the senior notes listed in the above table except for the Euro Notes for which interest is payable annually. We may redeem some or all of the senior notes of each series prior to their maturity, subject to certain restricïŋ―ons, and the payment of an applicable make-whole premium in certain instances. 

The senior notes rank pari passu with any other notes we may issue in the future pursuant to our commercial paper program (see addiïŋ―onal discussion regarding our commercial paper program below) and all exisïŋ―ng and future unsecured senior indebtedness of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on including the Revolving Credit Agreement and Bridge Credit Agreement, each as described further below. All exisïŋ―ng and future liabiliïŋ―es of the subsidiaries of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on are or will be effecïŋ―vely senior to the senior notes, any future borrowings pursuant to the Revolving Credit Agreement and borrowings made on June 8, 2022 under the Bridge Credit Agreement, and any future issuances of commercial paper notes. We were in compliance with all debt-related covenants at May 31, 2022. 

## **Credit Agreements** 

In March 2022, we entered into the following two credit agreements: 

- a $6.0 billion, five-year revolving credit agreement (the Revolving Credit Agreement), which provides for an unsecured $6.0 billion, five-year revolving credit facility (the Revolving Facility) to be used for our working capital purposes and for other general corporate purposes. Subject to certain condiïŋ―ons stated in the Revolving Credit Agreement, we may borrow, prepay and reborrow amounts under the Revolving Facility during the term of the Revolving Credit Agreement. All amounts borrowed under the Revolving Credit Agreement will become due on March 8, 2027, unless the commitments are terminated earlier either at our request or, if an event of default occurs, by the lenders (or automaïŋ―cally in the case of certain bankruptcy-related events). Interest is based on either (a) a Term Secured Overnight Financing Rate (SOFR)-based formula plus a margin of 87.5 basis points to 150.0 basis points, depending on the credit raïŋ―ng assigned to our long-term senior unsecured debt, or (b) a Base Rate formula plus a margin of 0.0 basis point to 50.0 basis points, depending on the same such credit raïŋ―ng, each as set forth in the Revolving Credit Agreement; and 

88 

Table of Contents Index to Financial Statements 

## **ORACLE CORPORATION** 

## **NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTSâ(Conïŋ―nued) May 31, 2022** 

- a $15.7 billion delayed draw term loan credit agreement (the Bridge Credit Agreement), which provides for an unsecured $15.7 billion, 364-day term loan commitment (the Bridge Facility), subject to the saïŋ―sfacïŋ―on of certain customary condiïŋ―ons. The Bridge Credit Agreement provides that, subject to certain excepïŋ―ons, net cash proceeds received by us from certain debt and equity issuances shall result in mandatory prepayments or commitment reducïŋ―ons under the Bridge Credit Agreement. The proceeds of borrowings under the Bridge Facility were used to finance the acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner, our refinancing of indebtedness in connecïŋ―on with such acquisiïŋ―on and to pay related fees and expenses. All amounts borrowed under the Bridge Credit Agreement will become due on March 7, 2023, unless seïŋ―led earlier pursuant to the terms of the Bridge Credit Agreement. Interest is based on either (a) a Term SOFR-based formula plus a margin of 100.0 basis points to 137.5 basis points, depending on the credit raïŋ―ng assigned to our long-term senior unsecured debt, or (b) a Base Rate formula plus a margin of 0.0 basis point to 37.5 basis points, depending on the same such credit raïŋ―ng, each as set forth in the Bridge Credit Agreement. 

No amounts were outstanding pursuant to either of the credit agreements as of May 31, 2022. On June 8, 2022, we drew down the full amount of the Bridge Credit Agreement to finance the acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner. 

Each of the abovemenïŋ―oned credit agreements contains certain customary representaïŋ―ons and warranïŋ―es, covenants and events of default, including the requirement that the raïŋ―o of âConsolidated EBITDAâ to âConsolidated Net Interest Expenseâ (each term as defined in the respecïŋ―ve credit agreements) of Oracle and its subsidiaries shall not be less than 3.0 to 1.0 at the end of any fiscal quarter during the period that the credit agreement is effecïŋ―ve. If an event of default occurs under one of the credit agreements and is not cured within applicable grace periods or waived, any unpaid amounts under the applicable credit agreement may be declared immediately due and payable and the commitments under that agreement may be terminated. We were in compliance with the two credit agreementsâ covenants as of May 31, 2022. 

## **Commercial Paper Program and Commercial Paper Notes** 

Our exisïŋ―ng $3.0 billion commercial paper program allows us to issue and sell unsecured short-term promissory notes pursuant to a private placement exempïŋ―on from the registraïŋ―on requirements under federal and state securiïŋ―es laws pursuant to dealer agreements with various banks and an Issuing and Paying Agency Agreement with Deutsche Bank Trust Company Americas. As of May 31, 2022 and 2021, we did not have any outstanding commercial paper notes.

## **Fiscal 2022 Oracle Restructuring Plan** 

During fiscal 2022, our management approved, commiïŋ―ed to and iniïŋ―ated plans to restructure and further improve efficiencies in our operaïŋ―ons due to our acquisiïŋ―ons and certain other operaïŋ―onal acïŋ―viïŋ―es (2022 Restructuring Plan). In the fourth quarter of fiscal 2022, our management supplemented the 2022 Restructuring Plan to reflect addiïŋ―onal acïŋ―ons that we expect to take. The total esïŋ―mated restructuring costs associated with the 2022 Restructuring Plan are up to $392 million and will be recorded to the restructuring expense line item within our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons as they are incurred. We recorded $223 million of restructuring expenses in connecïŋ―on with the 2022 Restructuring Plan in fiscal 2022 and we expect to incur the majority of the esïŋ―mated remaining $169 million through the end of fiscal 2023. Any changes to the esïŋ―mates or ïŋ―ming of execuïŋ―ng the 2022 Restructuring Plan will be reflected in our future results of operaïŋ―ons.

## **11. STOCKHOLDERSâ (DEFICIT) EQUITY** 

## **Common Stock Repurchases** 

Our Board of Directors has approved a program for us to repurchase shares of our common stock. On December 9, 2021, we announced that our Board of Directors approved an expansion of our stock repurchase program by an addiïŋ―onal $10.0 billion. As of May 31, 2022, approximately $9.4 billion remained available for stock repurchases pursuant to our stock repurchase program. We repurchased 185.8 million shares for $16.2 billion (including 0.3 million shares for $19 million that were repurchased but not seïŋ―led), 329.2 million shares for $21.0 billion, and 361.0 million shares for $19.2 billion in fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020, respecïŋ―vely, under the stock repurchase program. 

Our stock repurchase authorizaïŋ―on does not have an expiraïŋ―on date and the pace of our repurchase acïŋ―vity will depend on factors such as our working capital needs, our cash requirements for acquisiïŋ―ons and dividend payments, our debt repayment obligaïŋ―ons or repurchases of our debt, our stock price, and economic and market condiïŋ―ons. Our stock repurchases may be effected from ïŋ―me to ïŋ―me through open market purchases or pursuant to a Rule 10b5-1 plan. Our stock repurchase program may be accelerated, suspended, delayed or disconïŋ―nued at any ïŋ―me. 

## **Dividends on Common Stock** 

During fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020, our Board of Directors declared cash dividends of $1.28, $1.04 and $0.96 per share of our outstanding common stock, respecïŋ―vely, which we paid during the same period. 

In June 2022, our Board of Directors declared a quarterly cash dividend of $0.32 per share of our outstanding common stock. The dividend is payable on July 26, 2022 to stockholders of record as of the close of business on July 12, 2022. Future declaraïŋ―ons of dividends and the establishment of future record and payment dates are subject to the final determinaïŋ―on of our Board of Directors.

## **12. EMPLOYEE BENEFIT PLANS** 

## **Stock-Based Compensaïŋ―on Plans** 

## **Stock Plans** 

In fiscal 2021, we adopted the 2020 Equity Incenïŋ―ve Plan to replace the Amended and Restated 2000 Long-Term Equity Incenïŋ―ve Plan (the 2000 Plan) which provides for the issuance of long-term performance awards, including restricted stock-based awards, non-qualified stock opïŋ―ons and incenïŋ―ve stock opïŋ―ons, as well as stock purchase rights and stock appreciaïŋ―on rights, to our eligible employees, officers and directors who are also employees or consultants, independent consultants and advisers. In fiscal 2022, our stockholders, upon the recommendaïŋ―on of our Board of Directors (the Board), approved the adopïŋ―on of the Amended and Restated 2020 Equity Incenïŋ―ve Plan (the 2020 Plan and, together with the 2000 Plan, the Plans), which increased the number of authorized shares of stock that may be issued under the 2020 Plan by 300 million shares. 

The total number of shares authorized under the 2020 Plan is (i) 390 million shares, plus (ii) the number of shares that were unissued and available for grant under the 2000 Plan as of the date that the 2020 Plan was originally adopted, plus (iii) the number of shares granted and outstanding as of the date that the 2020 Plan was originally adopted which would have been available again for issuance under the terms of the 2000 Plan had the 2020 Plan not been adopted. Under the 2020 Plan, for each share granted as a full value award in the form of a restricted stock unit (RSU) or a performance-based restricted stock award (PSU), an equivalent of 2.5 shares is deducted from our pool of shares available for grant. 

As of May 31, 2022, 125 million unvested RSUs, 36 million performance-based stock opïŋ―ons (PSOs), of which 6 million shares were vested, and service-based stock opïŋ―ons (SOs) to purchase 60 million shares of common stock, of which 59 million shares were vested, were outstanding under the Plans. Approximately 371 million shares of common stock were available for future awards under the 2020 Plan as of May 31, 2022. To date, we have not issued any stock opïŋ―ons under the 2020 Plan or any stock purchase rights or stock appreciaïŋ―on rights under either of the Plans. 

The vesïŋ―ng schedule for all awards granted under the Plans is established by the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board. RSUs generally require service-based vesïŋ―ng of 25% annually over four years. SOs were previously granted under the 2000 Plan at not less than fair market value, become exercisable generally 25% annually over four years of service, and generally expire 10 years from the date of grant. 

PSOs granted under the 2000 Plan to our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer and Chief Technology Officer in fiscal 2018 consisted of seven numerically equivalent vesïŋ―ng tranches that potenïŋ―ally could vest. One tranche, which was based solely on the aïŋ―ainment of a market-based metric, was achieved and vested in fiscal 2022. Each of the remaining six tranches requires the aïŋ―ainment of both a performance metric and a market capitalizaïŋ―on metric by May 31, 2022, which was subsequently extended by three addiïŋ―onal fiscal years to May 31, 2025 via an amendment approved by the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board during fiscal 2022. If any of the remaining operaïŋ―onal and market capitalizaïŋ―on performance goals are achieved before May 31, 2025 addiïŋ―onal tranches may vest, assuming conïŋ―nued employment and service through the date the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board cerïŋ―fies that performance has been achieved. Upon amendment of the PSOs in fiscal 2022, we esïŋ―mated the revised fair values of the six unvested tranches of the PSOs using a Monte Carlo simulaïŋ―on approach. We are recognizing incremental stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense related to these amended awards for any of the remaining unvested tranches that are probable of achievement over the longer of the (a) esïŋ―mated implicit service period for performance-metric achievement, or (b) derived service period for market-based metric achievement. Stock-based compensaïŋ―on associated with a vesïŋ―ng tranche where vesïŋ―ng is no longer determined to be probable is reversed on a cumulaïŋ―ve basis and is no longer prospecïŋ―vely recognized in the period when such a determinaïŋ―on is made. We have preliminarily esïŋ―mated service periods for those tranches that have been deemed probable of achievement as of the amendment date to be approximately three to four years.

Parïŋ―cipants can generally contribute up to 40% of their eligible compensaïŋ―on on a per-pay-period basis as defined by the Oracle 401(k) Plan document or by the secïŋ―on 402(g) limit as defined by the U.S. Internal Revenue Service (IRS). We match a porïŋ―on of employee contribuïŋ―ons, currently 50% up to 6% of compensaïŋ―on each pay period, subject to maximum aggregate matching amounts. Our contribuïŋ―ons to the Oracle 401(k) Plan, net of forfeitures, were $164 million, $150 million and $152 million in fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020, respecïŋ―vely. 

We also offer non-qualified deferred compensaïŋ―on plans to certain employees whereby they may defer a porïŋ―on of their annual base and/or variable compensaïŋ―on unïŋ―l reïŋ―rement or a date specified by the employee in accordance with the plans. ## **13. INCOME TAXES** 

Our effecïŋ―ve tax rates for each of the periods presented are the result of the mix of income and losses earned in various tax jurisdicïŋ―ons that apply a broad range of income tax rates. Our (provision for) benefit from income taxes varied from that computed at the U.S. federal statutory income tax rate for fiscal 2022, 2021 and 2020 primarily due to earnings in foreign operaïŋ―ons, state taxes, the U.S. research and development tax credit, seïŋ―lements with tax authoriïŋ―es, the tax effects of stock-based compensaïŋ―on, the Foreign Derived Intangible Income deducïŋ―on and the tax effect of Global Intangible Low-Taxed Income. In addiïŋ―on, for fiscal 2021, our benefit from income taxes varied from the tax computed at the U.S. federal statutory income tax rate primarily due to a total net deferred tax benefit of $2.3 billion as a result of a parïŋ―al realignment of our legal enïŋ―ty structure that resulted in the intra-group transfer of certain intellectual property rights. 

In November 2021, the U.S. House of Representaïŋ―ves passed the âBuild Back Beïŋ―er Actâ budget reconciliaïŋ―on bill (the Bill). To date, the Bill has failed to advance in the Senate. If the Bill as currently draïŋ―ed (or a modified version containing similar revenue provisions) were enacted, it would substanïŋ―ally increase U.S. taxes on corporaïŋ―ons, including, among other changes, raising the level of U.S. tax on profits earned outside the U.S. and further restricïŋ―ng the deducïŋ―bility of interest expense. Such changes, if enacted, likely would have a material adverse impact on our future tax liabiliïŋ―es and consolidated financial results.

We provide for United States income taxes on the undistributed earnings and the other outside basis temporary differences of foreign subsidiaries unless they are considered indefinitely reinvested outside the United States. If the undistributed earnings and other outside basis differences were recognized in a taxable transacïŋ―on, they would generate foreign tax credits that would reduce the federal tax liability associated with the foreign dividend or the otherwise taxable transacïŋ―on. At May 31, 2022, assuming a full uïŋ―lizaïŋ―on of the foreign tax credits, the potenïŋ―al net deferred tax liability associated with these other outside basis temporary differences would be approximately $1.5 billion. 

Our net deferred tax assets were $6.8 billion and $5.8 billion as of May 31, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely. We believe that it is more likely than not that the net deferred tax assets will be realized in the foreseeable future. ## **14. SEGMENT INFORMATION** 

ASC 280, _Segment Reporïŋ―ng_ , establishes standards for reporïŋ―ng informaïŋ―on about operaïŋ―ng segments. Operaïŋ―ng segments are defined as components of an enterprise about which separate financial informaïŋ―on is available that is evaluated regularly by the chief operaïŋ―ng decision maker, or decision-making group, in deciding how to allocate resources and in assessing performance. Our chief operaïŋ―ng decision makers (CODMs) are our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer and Chief Technology Officer. We are organized by line of business and geographically. While our CODMs evaluate results in a number of different ways, the line of business management structure is the primary basis for which the allocaïŋ―on of resources and financial results are assessed. The tabular informaïŋ―on below presents financial informaïŋ―on that is provided to our CODMs for their review and assists our CODMs with evaluaïŋ―ng the companyâs performance and allocaïŋ―ng company resources. 

We have three businessesâcloud and license, hardware and servicesâeach of which is comprised of a single operaïŋ―ng segment. All three of our businesses market and sell our offerings globally to businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and resellers with a worldwide sales force posiïŋ―oned to offer the combinaïŋ―ons that best meet customer needs. 

Our cloud and license business engages in the sale, markeïŋ―ng and delivery of our enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies through cloud and on-premise deployment models including our cloud services and license support offerings; and our cloud license and on-premise license offerings. Cloud services and license support revenues are generated from offerings that are typically contracted with customers directly, billed to customers in advance, delivered to customers over ïŋ―me with our revenue recogniïŋ―on occurring over the contractual terms, and renewed by customers upon compleïŋ―on of the contractual terms. Cloud services and license support contracts provide customers with access to the latest updates to the applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies as they become available and for which the customer contracted and also include

## **15. EARNINGS PER SHARE** 

Basic earnings per share is computed by dividing net income for the period by the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding during the period. Diluted earnings per share is computed by dividing net income for the period by the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding during the period, plus the diluïŋ―ve effect of outstanding restricted stock-based awards, stock opïŋ―ons, and shares issuable under the employee stock purchase plan as applicable pursuant to the treasury stock method. The following table sets forth the computaïŋ―on of basic and diluted earnings per share:

|**(in millions, except per share data)**|**2022**||**2021**||**2020**||
|Net income<br>|$ 6,717||$ 13,746||$ 10,135||
|Weighted average common shares outstanding<br>||2,700||2,945||3,211|
|Diluïŋ―ve efect of employee stock plans<br>||86||77||83|

## **16. LEGAL PROCEEDINGS** 

## **Hewleïŋ―-Packard Company Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on** 

On June 15, 2011, Hewleïŋ―-Packard Company, now Hewleïŋ― Packard Enterprise Company (HP), filed a complaint in the California Superior Court, County of Santa Clara against Oracle Corporaïŋ―on alleging numerous causes of acïŋ―on including breach of contract, breach of the covenant of good faith and fair dealing, defamaïŋ―on, intenïŋ―onal interference with prospecïŋ―ve economic advantage and violaïŋ―on of the California Unfair Business Pracïŋ―ces Act. The complaint alleged that when Oracle announced on March 22 and 23, 2011 that it would no longer develop future versions of its soïŋ―ware to run on HPâs Itanium-based servers, it breached a seïŋ―lement agreement signed on September 20, 2010 (the HP Seïŋ―lement Agreement), resolving liïŋ―gaïŋ―on between HP and one of Oracleâs former CEOs who had previously acted as HPâs chief execuïŋ―ve officer and chairman of HPâs board of directors. HP sought a judicial declaraïŋ―on of the parïŋ―esâ rights and obligaïŋ―ons under the HP Seïŋ―lement Agreement and other equitable and monetary relief. Oracle answered the complaint and filed cross-claims. 

Aïŋ―er a bench trial on the meaning of the HP Seïŋ―lement Agreement, the court found that the HP Seïŋ―lement Agreement required Oracle to conïŋ―nue to develop certain of its soïŋ―ware products for use on HPâs Itanium-based servers at no cost to HP. The case proceeded to a jury trial in May 2016. On June 30, 2016, the jury returned a verdict in favor of HP on its claims for breach of contract and breach of the implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing and against Oracle on its cross-claims. The jury awarded HP $3.0 billion in damages. Under the courtâs rulings, HP is enïŋ―tled to post-judgment interest, but not pre-judgment interest, on this award. 

Aïŋ―er the trial court denied Oracleâs moïŋ―on for a new trial, Oracle filed a noïŋ―ce of appeal on January 17, 2017. On February 2, 2017, HP filed a noïŋ―ce of appeal of the trial courtâs denial of pre-judgment interest. Oral argument was held on May 27, 2021. On June 14, 2021, the Court of Appeal affirmed both the judgment against Oracle noted above, and the denial of pre-judgment interest. On June 29, 2021, Oracle filed a Peïŋ―ïŋ―on for Rehearing with the Court of Appeal, which was denied on July 8, 2021. On July 26, 2021, Oracle filed a Peïŋ―ïŋ―on for Review with the California Supreme Court, which was denied on September 29, 2021. 

During fiscal 2022, Oracle remiïŋ―ed the enïŋ―rety of the $3.0 billion judgment and related $1.7 billion of accrued post-judgment interest and awarded costs and recorded such amounts as acquisiïŋ―on related and other expenses as presented per our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. 

On January 27, 2022, Oracle filed a Peïŋ―ïŋ―on for a Writ of Cerïŋ―orari with the U.S. Supreme Court, which was denied on May 16, 2022. This maïŋ―er is now concluded. 

## **Derivaïŋ―ve Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on Concerning Oracleâs NetSuite Acquisiïŋ―on** 

On May 3 and July 18, 2017, two alleged stockholders filed separate derivaïŋ―ve lawsuits in the Court of Chancery of the State of Delaware, purportedly on Oracleâs behalf. Thereaïŋ―er, the court consolidated the two derivaïŋ―ve cases and designated the July 18, 2017 complaint as the operaïŋ―ve complaint. The consolidated lawsuit was brought against all the then-current members and one former member of our Board of Directors, and Oracle as a nominal defendant. Plainïŋ―ff alleged that the defendants breached their fiduciary duïŋ―es by causing Oracle to agree to purchase NetSuite Inc. (NetSuite) at an excessive price. The complaint sought (and the operaïŋ―ve complaint conïŋ―nues to seek) declaratory relief, unspecified monetary damages (including interest), and aïŋ―orneysâ fees and costs. The defendants filed a moïŋ―on to dismiss, which the court denied on March 19, 2018. 

On May 4, 2018, our Board of Directors established a Special Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee (the SLC) to invesïŋ―gate the allegaïŋ―ons in this derivaïŋ―ve acïŋ―on. Three nonemployee directors served on the SLC. On August 15, 2019, the SLC filed a leïŋ―er with the court, staïŋ―ng that the SLC believed that plainïŋ―ff should be allowed to proceed with the derivaïŋ―ve liïŋ―gaïŋ―on on behalf of Oracle. Aïŋ―er the SLC advised the Board that it had fulfilled its duïŋ―es and obligaïŋ―ons, the Board withdrew the SLCâs authority, except that the SLC maintained certain authority to respond to discovery requests in the liïŋ―gaïŋ―on.

Aïŋ―er plainïŋ―ff filed the July 18, 2017 complaint, an addiïŋ―onal plainïŋ―ff joined the case. The operaïŋ―ve complaint asserts claims for breach of fiduciary duty against our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer, our Chief Technology Officer, the estate of Mark Hurd (our former Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer who passed away on October 18, 2019), and two other members of our Board of Directors. On December 28, 2020, our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer, our Chief Technology Officer, and Oracle as a nominal defendant filed answers to the operaïŋ―ve complaint. 

Expert discovery has concluded. This Board member remains a defendant in this case. Trial is scheduled to commence on July 18, 2022. 

While Oracle conïŋ―nues to evaluate these claims, we do not believe this liïŋ―gaïŋ―on will have a material impact on our financial posiïŋ―on or results of operaïŋ―ons. 

## **Securiïŋ―es Class Acïŋ―on and Derivaïŋ―ve Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on Concerning Oracleâs Cloud Business** 

On August 10, 2018, a putaïŋ―ve class acïŋ―on, brought by an alleged stockholder of Oracle, was filed in the U.S. District Court for the Northern District of California against us, our Chief Technology Officer, our then-two Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officers, two other Oracle execuïŋ―ves, and one former Oracle execuïŋ―ve. As noted above, Mr. Hurd, one of our then-two Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officers, passed away on October 18, 2019. On March 8, 2019, plainïŋ―ff filed an amended complaint. Plainïŋ―ff alleges that the defendants made or are responsible for false and misleading statements regarding Oracleâs cloud business. Plainïŋ―ff further alleges that the former Oracle execuïŋ―ve engaged in insider trading. Plainïŋ―ff seeks a ruling that this case may proceed as a class acïŋ―on, and seeks damages, aïŋ―orneysâ fees and costs, and unspecified declaratory/injuncïŋ―ve relief. On April 19, 2019, defendants moved to dismiss plainïŋ―ffâs amended complaint. On December 17, 2019, the court granted this moïŋ―on, giving plainïŋ―ffs an opportunity to file an amended complaint, which plainïŋ―ff filed on February 17, 2020. On April 23, 2020, defendants filed a moïŋ―on to dismiss, and the court held a hearing on this moïŋ―on on September 24, 2020. On March 22, 2021, the court granted in part and denied in part this moïŋ―on. The court dismissed the acïŋ―on as to one Oracle execuïŋ―ve and the former Oracle execuïŋ―ve. The court permiïŋ―ed plainïŋ―ff to proceed with only a narrow omissions theory against the remaining defendants. On April 21, 2021, defendants filed an answer to the complaint. On October 8, 2021, plainïŋ―ffs filed a moïŋ―on for class cerïŋ―ficaïŋ―on, which the court granted on May 9, 2022. On May 23, 2022, defendants filed a peïŋ―ïŋ―on in the Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals for permission to appeal the courtâs order granïŋ―ng class cerïŋ―ficaïŋ―on, and plainïŋ―ffs filed an opposiïŋ―on on June 2, 2022. On June 3, 2022, the court âSo Orderedâ a sïŋ―pulaïŋ―on by the parïŋ―es, which vacated all dates in this case because the parïŋ―es had reached an agreement to seïŋ―le this acïŋ―on, subject to the courtâs approval. On June 8, 2022, the Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals granted defendantsâ unopposed moïŋ―on to stay the peïŋ―ïŋ―on for permission to appeal in light of the proposed seïŋ―lement. 

On February 12 and May 8, 2019, two stockholder derivaïŋ―ve lawsuits were filed in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California. The cases were consolidated, and on July 8, 2019, a single plainïŋ―ff filed a consolidated complaint. The consolidated complaint brought various claims relaïŋ―ng to the 10b-5 class acïŋ―on described immediately above. The parïŋ―es agreed to stay the derivaïŋ―ve case pending resoluïŋ―on of defendantsâ moïŋ―on to dismiss the securiïŋ―es case, which the court granted in part and denied in part on March 22, 2021. 

Plainïŋ―ff filed an amended complaint on June 4, 2021. The derivaïŋ―ve suit is brought by an alleged stockholder of Oracle, purportedly on Oracleâs behalf, against our Chief Technology Officer, our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer, and the estate of Mark Hurd. Plainïŋ―ff claims that the alleged acïŋ―ons described in the class acïŋ―on discussed above caused harm to Oracle, and that defendants violated their fiduciary duïŋ―es of candor, good faith, loyalty, and due care by

## **Acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner Corporaïŋ―on and Related Borrowings** 

On June 8, 2022, pursuant to the terms of the tender offer and applicable Delaware law, we acquired all of the outstanding shares of Cernerâs common stock and effectuated the merger of Cerner with and into a wholly-owned subsidiary of Oracle, and Cerner became an indirect, wholly-owned subsidiary of Oracle. The iniïŋ―al purchase accounïŋ―ng for this transacïŋ―on has not yet been completed given the short period of ïŋ―me between the acquisiïŋ―on date and issuance of these consolidated financial statements and the financial results of Cerner will be included in our consolidated financial statements from the date of the acquisiïŋ―on. Refer to Note 2 above for more informaïŋ―on about our acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner. 

In connecïŋ―on with the acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner: 

- we borrowed $15.7 billion on June 8, 2022 pursuant to the Bridge Credit Agreement. The amount is due and payable in full on March 7, 2023 unless seïŋ―led earlier pursuant to the terms of the Bridge Credit Agreement. Addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on with respect to the Bridge Credit Agreement is included in Note 7 above; and 

- we assumed $1.6 billion of senior notes and other borrowings, of which $1.5 billion were paid on June 8, 2022.

## **AMENDED AND RESTATED** 

## **ORACLE CORPORATION EMPLOYEE STOCK PURCHASE PLAN (1992)** 

## **(as amended and restated on May 3, 2022)** 

The following consïŋ―tute the provisions of the Amended and Restated Oracle Corporaïŋ―on Employee Stock Purchase Plan (1992), which was originally adopted on August 24, 1992, and was amended and restated on March 22, 2002, February 8, 2005, October 1, 2009 and May 3, 2022.  This version of the Plan is effecïŋ―ve on and aïŋ―er October 1, 2022.  For Offering Periods under the Plan ending on or before September 30, 2022, refer to the version of the Plan as in effect for the applicable Offering Period. 

## **1. PURPOSE** 

This Plan is established to provide employees of Oracle and other Group Companies with an opportunity to purchase Common Stock through accumulated payroll deducïŋ―ons. It is the intenïŋ―on of Oracle that the Plan qualify as an âEmployee Stock Purchase Planâ under Secïŋ―on 423 of the Code. The provisions of the Plan shall, accordingly, be construed so as to extend and limit parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on in a manner consistent with the requirements of that secïŋ―on of the Code.  In addiïŋ―on, the Plan authorizes the grant of opïŋ―ons under a non-423 plan which do not qualify under Secïŋ―on 423 of the Code pursuant to rules, procedures or sub-plans adopted by Oracle designed to achieve desired tax or other objecïŋ―ves in parïŋ―cular locaïŋ―ons outside the United States.  The term âPlanâ used herein applies to both the Secïŋ―on 423 plan and the non-423 plan. 

Unless otherwise determined by the Board, each offering under the Plan in which Employees of Oracle and one or more Parïŋ―cipaïŋ―ng Subsidiaries may parïŋ―cipate shall be deemed a separate offering for purposes of Secïŋ―on 423 of the Code, even if the dates of the applicable Offering Periods of each such offering are idenïŋ―cal, and the provisions of the Plan shall separately apply to each offering.  The terms of such separate offerings need not be idenïŋ―cal provided that all Employees granted opïŋ―ons in a parïŋ―cular offering shall have the same rights and privileges in accordance with Secïŋ―on 16 below, except as otherwise may be permiïŋ―ed by Secïŋ―on 423 of the Code. 

## **2. DEFINITIONS** 

- (a) _âAffiliateâ_ means (i) any Subsidiary and (ii) any other enïŋ―ty in which Oracle has a controlling equity interest.

## **4. OFFERING PERIODS**

In no event, however, will any such Offering Period be longer than twenty-seven (27) months. 

## **5. PARTICIPATION**

## **6. PAYROLL DEDUCTIONS**

3 

(c) All payroll deducïŋ―ons made by a parïŋ―cipant shall be credited to his or her account under the Plan. ## **7. GRANT OF OPTION** 

(a) On the Offering Date of each Offering Period, each eligible Employee parïŋ―cipaïŋ―ng in the Plan shall be granted an opïŋ―on to purchase (at the per share opïŋ―on price) up to a number of shares of Common Stock determined by dividing such Employeeâs payroll deducïŋ―ons or contribuïŋ―ons to be accumulated during such Offering Period by ninety-five percent (95%) of the fair market value of a share of Common Stock on the Exercise Date, provided that the number of shares subject to the opïŋ―on will be limited to 200% of the number of shares determined by dividing the amount accumulated in the employeesâ payroll deducïŋ―ons/contribuïŋ―on account by 95% of the fair market value of a share of Common Stock on the Offering Date, subject to the limitaïŋ―ons set forth in Secïŋ―ons 3(b) and 11 hereof. (b) The opïŋ―on price per share of the shares offered in a given Offering Period shall be 95% of the fair market value of a share of the Common Stock on the Exercise Date. Unless otherwise determined by the Board, the fair market value of Common Stock on a given date shall be the closing price from the previous business dayâs trading on the New York Stock Exchange.

## **8. EXERCISE OF OPTION** 

Unless a parïŋ―cipant withdraws from the Plan or terminates employment as provided in Secïŋ―on 10, his or her opïŋ―on for the purchase of shares will be exercised automaïŋ―cally on the Exercise Date of the Offering Period and the maximum number of shares subject to opïŋ―on will be purchased for him or her at the applicable opïŋ―on price with the accumulated payroll deducïŋ―ons or contribuïŋ―ons in his or her account.  No fracïŋ―onal shares of Common Stock may be issued pursuant to an opïŋ―on to purchase shares of Common Stock.  During his or her lifeïŋ―me, a parïŋ―cipantâs opïŋ―on to purchase shares hereunder is exercisable only by him or her. 

## **9. DELIVERY** 

(a) As soon as pracïŋ―cable aïŋ―er the Exercise Date of each Offering Period, Oracle shall arrange for the electronic delivery to each parïŋ―cipant, as appropriate, of the shares purchased upon exercise of his or her opïŋ―on. Any cash remaining to the credit of a parïŋ―cipantâs account under the Plan aïŋ―er a purchase by him or her of shares at the terminaïŋ―on of each Offering Period under the Plan which is insufficient to purchase a full share of Common Stock, will be refunded, without interest (unless required by local law as determined by the Board), to him or her as soon as pracïŋ―cable.  The Board also may return cash remaining in each parïŋ―cipantâs payroll deducïŋ―on or contribuïŋ―on account, without interest (unless required by local law as determined by the Board), if a purchase of shares will not occur because the Board determines such purchase is not feasible or that the condiïŋ―ons for the issuance of shares have not been met.

## **10. WITHDRAWAL: TERMINATION OR TRANSFER OF EMPLOYMENT** 

(a) A parïŋ―cipant may withdraw all but not less than all the payroll deducïŋ―ons credited to his or her account under the Plan at any ïŋ―me prior to the Exercise Date of the Offering Period prior to the fiïŋ―eenth (15th) day of the last month of the Offering Period. 5 

(b) In the event that a parïŋ―cipantâs employment with Oracle or another Group Company terminates for any reason (including death, disability, or reïŋ―rement), or if a parïŋ―cipant becomes otherwise ineligible to parïŋ―cipate in the Plan, in either case, on or prior to the fiïŋ―eenth (15th) day of the last month of an Offering Period, the payroll deducïŋ―ons credited to his or her account will be returned as soon as pracïŋ―cable and without interest (except where required by local law as determined by the Board) to him or her or, in the case of his or her death, to the executor or administrator of the estate of the parïŋ―cipant, and his or her opïŋ―on will be automaïŋ―cally terminated. In the event that a parïŋ―cipantâs employment with Oracle or another Group Company terminates for any reason or a parïŋ―cipant becomes otherwise ineligible to parïŋ―cipate in the Plan aïŋ―er such date, the parïŋ―cipantâs payroll deducïŋ―ons credited to his or her account will be used to purchase stock on the Exercise Date for that Offering Period and his or her parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on will end at the beginning of the next Offering Period. 

(c) In the event an Employee fails to conïŋ―nue to meet the eligibility requirements of an Employee (as defined in Secïŋ―on 2(f)) during the enïŋ―re Offering Period, other than as set forth in Secïŋ―on 10(d) below, he or she will be deemed to have elected to withdraw from the Plan and the payroll deducïŋ―ons credited to his or her account will be returned to him or her as soon as pracïŋ―cable and without interest (except where required by local law as determined by the Board) and his or her opïŋ―on will be automaïŋ―cally terminated.
